Fourth Board Meeting of the International Society 105

And Invitation to Pei Fuhang for a Lecture

According to the Central News Agency, the International Society, since its registration with the Central Public Movement Guidance Committee, has been actively carrying out its affairs. The society held its fourth board meeting at the Sino-French Friendship Association on Route Lafayette at 2 PM yesterday, and invited Pei Fuhang, the president of the National Shanghai College of Commerce, to give a lecture entitled "The Attitude of Cultural Movement Advocates." Attendees included all board members such as Wang Shanji, Xu Shipu, Li Lixia, and Yang Li. Liu Chuanzhong chaired the meeting, Gu Gaoyang served as the recorder, and Shen Zuru reported on the cultural movement situation. Wang Shanji and He Xueni reported on the society's affairs, followed by Pei Fuhang's lecture. Finally, resolutions were discussed and recorded as follows:

Pei's Lecture briefly stated that in recent decades, the domestic cultural movement has repeatedly failed because those engaged in the cultural movement either made empty promises without being practical, falling into the pedantic and empty shortcomings of Song Confucian commentary, or advocated for practical learning, engaging in textual research and exegesis, following the old habits of Han scholars who did not discuss matters of principle, in order to avoid the realities of the environment. Both of these approaches were of no benefit to the real society. Therefore, past cultural movements flourished for a time, but morale continued to decline, and the national situation was on the verge of collapse. Those engaged in cultural work in the future should change their past mistakes and take the practical learning spirit of Yan Xizhai in the early Qing Dynasty as the standard, that is, learning and thought should be integrated with life and behavior. Apart from practice and practical work, there is no such thing as learning, which is also the spirit of practical work and vigorous action advocated by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. All cultural movement advocates, as long as everyone can start from their own behavior, can naturally achieve practical results. The current domestic cultural movement, centered on the New Life Movement, should be practical and personally practice it, and should no longer deceive with empty words. In short, as long as the cultural route is clearly identified, it should be implemented without empty talk or evasion of reality. This is the correct attitude for cultural movement advocates. He wished to offer this idea to the comrades of the society and wished the society a bright future.

Resolutions (1) It is recommended to the Central Government to instruct all specialized schools and above in the country to add lectures on Japanese issues, and Wang Shanji and Zhang Shiyuan are delegated to draft the reasons and methods, and submit them to the Standing Committee for review and issuance. (2) The following issues will be the focus of discussion for the society recently: 1. The impact of the Soviet Union's joining the League of Nations on the Far East; 2. The Central European issue; 3. The revival of the Anglo-Japanese alliance; 4. The pros and cons of our government increasing silver export taxes. (3) Invite Pei Fuhang, Wu Songgao, Tao Xisheng, Xiong Mengfei, Zhang Songnian, Zhang Yuanruo, Luo Dunwei, Gang Hengyi and other gentlemen to be honorary directors of the society. (4) Member Wen Guangyi of this society will go to the UK, and Wen should be designated to be responsible for organizing the London branch of the society in London.

Shipping Guild and Four Other Groups Commemorate Navigator Sha Huijia Yesterday 106

Zhang Chuqing Presides Over the Ceremony, Yu Qiaqing and Others Give Speeches

The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association, Fuzhou Changan Steamship Company, China Merchant Ship Officers Association, and Wusong Fisheries School Alumni Association held a memorial service for the young navigator Sha Huijia at the Lake Society Hall on Guizhou Road at 2 PM yesterday. Yu Qiaqing, Zhang Chuqing, Jin Yueshi, Hou Zongqing, Zhang Junyi, Yang Yue'an, Chen Zhongping, Zhang Jidan, Yu Angxiao, Yu Zhuyun, Wang Yunfu, Qian Cangshuo, Bao Yuqiu and others, totaling more than 200 people, attended. Zhang Chuqing, the principal of Wusong Fisheries School, presided over the ceremony. After the music was played and the sacrifice was made, Zhang Junyi reported on Sha's life, detailing Sha's intelligence and diligence when he was at school, and his outstanding achievements after graduation. Then, Yu Qiaqing, a leader in the shipping industry, Jin Yueshi, a pioneer in the officers industry, and Hou Zongqing, a technician from the Ministry of Industry, gave speeches one after another, expressing their regret over Sha's death, and encouraging their surviving comrades to continue their efforts in order to achieve the goal of fully regaining navigation rights. Yu's speech lasted for an hour, recounting his 40 years of hard work in the shipping industry and the various processes of striving for the status of Chinese officers, which was particularly sincere and moving. Yu concluded by saying that Sha's death was not only a misfortune for his individual and his family, but also a great loss to our country's shipping industry. Finally, Sha's brother, Sha Yujia of the Sanbei Company, led his family to express their gratitude, and the memorial service presented the guests with a portrait of Sha as a memento. Then the music was played and the ceremony was completed. Sha graduated from Wusong Fisheries School in 1911 and served in the navigation industry for more than ten years. Two years ago, he joined the Shanghai Pilot Association as a pilot and also served as a member of the Shanghai Maritime Administration Bureau's Ship Collision and Dispute Resolution Committee. His academic ability and talent were admired by both Chinese and foreigners. Unfortunately, he passed away this summer at the age of 31. Everyone, whether they knew him or not, mourned the loss of a backbone figure in our country's shipping industry. Yesterday, the memorial hall was filled with words of mourning, with almost no space left. Yu Qiaqing, Du Yuesheng, Liu Hongsheng, Zhang Xiaoruo, Yuan Ludeng, Zhao Yuntai and others from the shipping industry, Jiao Dingxi, Chen Ganqing, Jin Yueshi and others from the navigation industry, and relatives, teachers and friends Xia Yiting, Qin Yuan, Yang Ying and others all sent wreaths and elegiac scrolls.

The Results of the Japanese Goods Sample Exhibition Were a Major Failure 107

The Japanese Newspaper Reports That It Failed to Attract Chinese People

Participating Stores Returned Disappointed

According to the Japanese-language Daily News yesterday, the sample exhibition initiated by the Wholesale Guidance Society was held on the 8th at the original site of the Beifu Department Store. More than 50 general merchandise stores from Tokyo, Osaka, Nagoya, and other places participated in the exhibition. Initially, it was originally scheduled to be held at the Yipinsan Hotel, but it was changed due to opposition from the Chinese side. At that time, various operators had various discussions, and some felt that this trial opening was quite important. As a result, it was a major failure. However, the newspaper reports all said that the sample market was a great success, and even the goods sold amounted to more than 300,000 yuan, and the future prospects were very optimistic. The general public believed it to be true. Who knew that in reality, the contracts signed during the three-day sample market by various participating groups who stayed in Shanghai for more than ten days did not reach 20,000 yuan, which was less than one-tenth of the claimed 300,000 yuan. The main reason for its great failure was that the change of address from Yipinsan Hotel to the original site of Beifu Department Store resulted in Chinese merchants all holding back. As a result, the planned plan was completely shattered. Although 2,000 people were invited, the Chinese people mostly visited and left, and there was hardly any negotiation or sales. Therefore, all the participating stores returned disappointed. This was due to the failure to recognize the situation in the Chinese market, but it was also due to the recession in mainland China. Only Japanese exporters to China, misled by the timing, suffered this unexpected adverse effect, and were dissatisfied by those who argued that the timing was too early.

Catholic Church Held Global Mission Day Yesterday 108

The Catholic Church has been spreading around the world for nineteen centuries. At present, the number of believers has reached more than 400 million. In addition to the majority of developed countries in Europe and the United States, there are more than 300 dioceses in the missionary areas of Asia, Africa, and Australia. About 20,000 priests are engaged in missionary work in distant places. If we include the male and female monks and teachers who assist, there are as many as 220,000 people. The religious, educational, and charitable undertakings they run, only counting within the missionary area, have 56,300 large and small churches, more than 37,300 men's and women's schools, more than 2,289,000 male and female students, more than 770 hospitals, more than 36,300 hospital beds, more than 110 leprosariums, 12,800 hospital beds, more than 1,970 orphanages, more than 113,000 orphans, more than 430 nursing homes, more than 17,700 elderly people, and countless other similar good deeds. The cost of their establishment and maintenance is very large, and relies on the generous donations of believers. The former Pope Benedict XV, in order to encourage believers to enthusiastically support missionary work, designated the second Sunday before the end of October each year as Mission Day. Missionary organizations in all countries around the world have obeyed and enthusiastically held it. The current Pope Pius XI is enthusiastic about missionary work, and his achievements are remarkable. He has repeatedly ordered the world to expand publicity. This year, Archbishop Cai Ning came to China to represent the Pope in managing church affairs. Cai had previously worked in the Propaganda Headquarters of the Roman Catholic Church for many years, and was very enthusiastic about supporting missionary work. In addition to the declaration issued by Secretary-General Jiang translated into Chinese and distributed, he also personally sent official letters to the leaders of dioceses across the country, calling for unanimous and enthusiastic holding of the event. The Catholic churches in Shanghai have already done this. In the Mass yesterday morning (the 21st), the priests of each church gave speeches on the importance of missionary work. In addition to instructing believers to pray enthusiastically, they also encouraged the public to donate generously to missionary expenses, or set up donation boxes in the church, or send students to solicit donations on the spot. The money will be sent by the head priests of each church to Bishop Hui in this district, and then sent to the Propaganda Headquarters in Rome, where the minister will allocate it to missionary areas around the world according to the needs of each diocese. On this day, the Vatican Radio Station used multiple languages to broadcast missionary speeches to the world to spread publicity.

Xiong Case Scheduled for Trial 109

After the reactionary element Xiong Guohua surrendered, he was assassinated by rioters sent by the Communist Party in the Qianji Hotel where Xiong was staying last month. Xiong was shot and injured, and the police sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment and assigned a detective to monitor him in the hospital. Unexpectedly, the rioters broke into the hospital ward again, killed Xiong with a pistol, and also shot and killed the resident detective and a Chinese constable sent by the French police to the hospital to treat the patient. After the incident, the police organs were extremely active, hoping to catch the murderer as soon as possible. Soon, within a day or two after the incident, ten male and female criminals were captured one after another, and a secret party's organization was uncovered on the third floor of the Xinwenxiang Silver Shop in the French Concession. Twenty-seven pistols, two bombs, a steel vest, and many reactionary printed materials were seized on the spot. They have been twice handed over to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court for review, but both times were deemed to be important and forbade public attendance during the investigation period. Now, it is heard that the male and female criminals in the entire case have been secretly interrogated by the Second Branch of the Higher Court twice. The Municipal Public Security Bureau believes that these people have also committed major crimes in the Chinese territory, and specially prepared a document by Director Wen, consulting the Second Branch of the Higher Court to allow the criminals to be temporarily taken away by the Public Security Bureau for investigation. Later, when the bureau concluded the interrogation and sent them back to the Second Branch of the Higher Court, the French Concession police stated that since a large number of weapons were found in the French Concession, the criminals must have also committed violence in the French Concession, so they also sent a letter to the court after the Public Security Bureau, requesting the court to allow the criminals to be taken to the Third Branch of the Higher Court. After several investigations and interrogations, the trial has now been completed. A few days ago, they were still sent back to the Second Branch of the Higher Court and handed over to the police and women's prison for detention separately. The Second Branch of the Higher Court has also scheduled the trial to begin officially on the 29th of this month. At this trial, the police will list the crimes obtained from the investigation and file a lawsuit in accordance with the law. At that time, if there are no special reasons, the trial may be open to the public, and those with tickets will be allowed to attend.

Severe Drought in Tongxiang County, County Magistrate Comes to Shanghai to Raise Relief Funds 110

The Tongxiang County in Zhejiang Province is adjacent to Haining and Haiyan. This summer, the drought has been extraordinarily severe. The rivers have dried up and turned into barren land. The fields are cracked and unable to be sown. All agricultural by-products have withered. The disaster victims are selling their children to cook food and begging for food. Suicides by the whole family are often heard, which is very pitiful. The local officials and local gentry first raised funds in the interior, but due to the continuous commercial depression in recent years, it is difficult to collect large amounts of money. Therefore, in order to raise relief funds widely, the legal groups jointly elected Liu Jiahhou, the representative of the county party department, Shen Guangxiong, the county magistrate, and the gentry Shen Qiluo and Shen Songsheng, etc., to come to Shanghai to discuss emergency relief measures with the fellow villagers in Shanghai. Lu Jianquan, Xu Guannan, and Xu Xiaoxia invited the fellow villagers in Shanghai to gather at Xu's residence on North Zhejiang Road for discussion. Attendees included County Magistrate Shen, Shen Songsheng, Liu Jiahhou, Guang Qiluo, Lu Jianquan, Xu Guannan, Xu Xiaoxia, Xu Xuying, Lu Feibo, Shen Luyi, Yan Shaohe, Yan Duhe, Cheng Zhihe, Cheng Muxian, Chen Kuisheng, Zhang Zounong, Zhang Zhuxian, Hu Yangqian, Xu Pinshao, Xia Jinhou and other more than a dozen people. First, County Magistrate Shen presided over the meeting, reporting on the failure of the initial relief efforts to pump water and the provincial plan, and requesting the fellow villagers abroad to assist in disaster relief. Liu Jiahhou then stated that the disaster in the county was serious, and the tragic situation was unprecedented in nearly a hundred years. It was decided on the spot that the current priority is to raise emergency relief funds and distribute rice. As for the future implementation of work relief, including the county's water conservancy and other matters, funds will be allocated by the provincial government for further discussion. Currently, only two items, the distribution of wheat seeds and rice, have been reduced in scope. Even with a smaller plan, it is still impossible to do without 100,000 yuan. In fact, there are more than 40,000 people in the county who cannot survive without relief. Donation registration books were filled out on the spot, and a total of 4,150 yuan was obtained. This is a drop in the bucket and still does not solve the problem. Therefore, the donation registration books were distributed again, asking the fellow villagers abroad to be responsible for soliciting donations. The other fellow villagers are scattered abroad and their addresses are unknown. After verification, the donation registration books will be sent by letter one after another. It was also agreed that the communication address and collection address of the disaster relief association in Shanghai would be Xu's residence at No. 61, Beizhejiang Road, North of the Old Garbage Bridge in Shanghai. At the same time, Zhang Zhuxian and Xia Jinhou were appointed as general affairs of the documents to jointly plan the progress.

County Government Meeting to Organize Baojia System 112

Decision to Implement on November 1

The Shanghai County Government recently received an order from the province to organize the baojia system throughout the county from November 1. Since the deadline stipulated in the provincial order was approaching, it convened a meeting the day before to discuss the methods. The chiefs of various districts and the head of the First Section, Wang Xuepeng, the technical director Qi Kezhong, and the county magistrate Pan Zhongjia attended the meeting, and Cao Yuanxun took the minutes. Matters for discussion (1) Draft the budget for the compilation and investigation of baojia, and it was resolved to amend and approve it. (2) In accordance with the regulations, the schedule for the formation of baojia is as follows: the first phase is 20 days, the second phase is 50 days, and the third phase is 50 days, for a total of four months. The area of this county is less than 500 square miles, and the population is less than 26,000 households, and the self-raised funds are extremely tight. Should the deadline for compilation and investigation be shortened to 75 days, the first phase is 15 days, the second phase is 30 days, and the third phase is 30 days, so as to complete the work as soon as possible and save costs? The proposal was resolved and passed. (3) Decide on the date to start the compilation and investigation. It was resolved to set November 1. (4) The past neighborhood organization of this county is relatively complete. Can the existing neighborhood be reorganized this time? The proposal was resolved and passed. (5) In accordance with the regulations, before starting the baojia, the chiefs of each district, the assistants of the district, and the compilation and investigation committee members should be convened to hold a training course to teach the significance of the formation of baojia. How should the aforementioned training course be organized? It was resolved to convene before the 25th of this month. (6) Should each district convene township chiefs to hold training courses so that they can thoroughly understand the significance and procedures of the baojia? It was resolved to be convened separately by each district. (7) How should this county widely publicize the compilation and investigation of baojia? It was resolved that in addition to printing slogans and publicizing to the public, the Education Bureau should be ordered to instruct all schools and social education institutions in the county to do their best to publicize it, and publish a special issue on baojia.

The South District Rent Reduction Association Petitions the Executive Yuan to Resolve the Rent Reduction 113

Rent Reduction Disputes Open Up Unprecedented Litigation

Earnestly Instructing and Comforting the Desire of the Whole Shanghai Citizens

The South District Rent Reduction Association submitted a document to the Executive Yuan, saying: "We are submitting this document because the rent reduction dispute is becoming increasingly serious. We earnestly request that you give clear instructions to comfort the people." We once, in a fast mail telegram on August 5, outlined the depression in Shanghai and the difficulty in bearing the heavy rent. We hope that you will clearly reduce the rent to relieve the people. Now, if this is prolonged, it will cause a rent litigation that has never been seen in China, and the feelings between the host and the guest will be hurt more and more, and the situation will become increasingly worse. If we look at Shanghai superficially, its boats and vehicles are crowded and people are bustling, but in fact, the prices are reduced to seek sales, and the goods are sold out. The north and south cities are all the same. This is actually because the shops are trying their best to support it in order to decorate the first-class commercial port and plan for its future recovery. Moreover, Shanghai has always been known as an inch of gold. Even if it is a snail's house, the rent is strangely expensive. Anyone who travels to Shanghai knows this. In addition, recently, various businesses have fallen sharply. Some have stopped and closed, and even more have tightened. They have been forced to dismiss employees and reduce salaries in order to maintain the status quo. Therefore, the current market situation in Shanghai, although golden and jade on the outside, is actually ruined on the inside. Moreover, the four major needs of life are clothing, food, housing, and transportation. Clothing, food, and transportation can still be saved, but the matter of housing cannot allow the whole family to live in the open every day. We are following the legacy of President Sun Yat-sen and entrusted by the citizens to run around and appeal, hoping to help businesses and revitalize Shanghai. However, the landlords who see profit and forget righteousness all use real estate as speculation and ignore President Sun Yat-sen's principle of people's livelihood. This is very painful. Now, we have found that rent reductions in the capital, Anqing, have been implemented long ago, and Hangzhou in Zhejiang is also planning to implement it by the municipal government. Although the Shanghai municipal government has already understood the people's difficulties, it has not made a correct statement, resulting in the citizens' public anger under the coercion of the wealthy, stopping payment of rent and depositing it in the bank on a monthly basis, waiting for a solution. However, the landlords who are good at litigation often file lawsuits on the grounds of rent resistance. Fortunately, the government and the court deeply understand this and deal with it with love and peace. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, in the midst of military affairs, still thinks of the people of Shanghai who are suffering. You are a veteran of the party and the country and a star of the people's fortune. In all the past things, all the actions that benefit the country and the people have been carried out with the spirit of "If I don't jump into the fire pit, who will jump into the fire pit? If I don't go to hell, who will go to hell?" as the vanguard of the people. Now, we have to report the suffering of the citizens and the fact of the city's depression, hoping that you will care about the people's suffering, rescue the people's livelihood, and give clear instructions to order the Shanghai municipal government to resolve it quickly, so as to relieve the people's difficulties and revitalize the city's appearance, and to comfort the 3 million residents of Shanghai who are in deep trouble. This is a matter of both public virtue and convenience. We respectfully present this document to Wang, the president of the Executive Yuan."

He would stay in Anhui for a short time to organize everything. They talked for about an hour before taking their leave. It is said that Liu has already departed by night train last night and will arrive in Tunxi tomorrow. The association has sent telegrams to various organizations in Huizhou to prepare a welcome.

Inauguration of the Xuegeng Hall at the YMCA 120

The Shanghai YMCA, because the late General Secretary Cao Xuegeng was one of the founders of the association and served for more than 20 years, making great contributions to the association and society, specially opened a hall on the second floor of the new association building at Eight Immortals Bridge, named Xuegeng Hall. They also commissioned Mr. Fuji Shirō to cast a bronze statue and a commemorative monument to commemorate him forever. Yesterday (the 21st) at 3 p.m., the inauguration ceremony of Xuegeng Hall was held, with orderly arrangements and great solemnity.

Guests Attending: In addition to all the directors, staff, and family members of Cao, there were more than 600 Chinese and foreign people from all walks of life, including Wang Zhengting, Gao Fengchi, Yu Zuoting, Song Hanzhang, Pan Gong_, Wu Kaisheng, Li Dachao, Li Zhaozhao_, Li Denghui, Chen Guangfu, Zhao Jinqing, Ding Shujing, Pei Zhengyong, Pei Yunqing, Mi Xingru, Ge Laien, Zheng Xiangheng, Liang Xiaochu, Wu Qingtai, Yan Fuqing, etc.

Order of the Meeting: The meeting first opened in the auditorium of the association. Everyone sang a memorial song, Dr. Ge Laien offered a prayer, General Secretary Lu Ganchen of the association delivered an opening speech, Dr. Wang Zhengting gave a speech, the Moore Memorial Church Choir sang, Mr. Gao Fengchi spoke about Cao's achievements, and Mr. Cao Maode (Cao Xuegeng's eldest son) gave a reply. Then, the inauguration ceremony of Xuegeng Hall was held. The Moore Memorial Church Choir sang, Song Hanzhang and Luo Weilian unveiled the plaque, Yu Pugeng played a solo, Dr. Ge Laien gave a blessing, and the meeting adjourned after a group photo.

Portrait of the Late Cao Xuegeng

Wang's Speech: Gathering today in this hall of great men, one cannot help but think of the small and narrow spaces of the YMCA on Suzhou Road, Beijing Road, and Nanjing Road in the past. How could there be such success today without the great contributions of Mr. Cao? Mr. Cao served the YMCA for more than 20 years, truly working hard and achieving great merit. It was not easy to bring the YMCA to this point, so it is worthy of our commemoration. His strengths as a person can also serve as a model for us. He had perseverance, willpower, and did not avoid difficulties. He served the YMCA for more than 20 years, never slacking off, and eventually became ill due to his hard work. The YMCA has such a solid foundation today entirely because of the meticulous organization of Mr. Cao in the past. Therefore, Mr. Cao is a good example for us and a good example for the Chinese people.

Cao's Biography: Cao Xigeng, also known as Cao Xuegeng, was from Jiaxing. He was born on November 16, 1873. His father, Zibin, was a famous pastor of the Methodist Church, renowned in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. His mother, née Yan, was the aunt of the current Ambassador Yan Huiqing. Cao grew up in Suzhou. After graduating from elementary school, he studied at a certain high school in Kobe, Japan. After returning to China, he entered St. John's University and graduated in 1893. He then became a teacher at the Zhongxi Academy. In 1898, Louis from the United States came to Shanghai to establish the YMCA. Cao strongly supported its establishment, planning and managing it, and his contributions were particularly great. In 1900, at the request of the directors and members of the YMCA, Cao officially became the general secretary of the association. After taking office, he made many reforms, such as establishing a middle school, purchasing land for the association buildings on Sichuan Road and Eight Immortals Bridge, and building the youth building of the West Sichuan Road association building. These are his most prominent achievements. As for the construction of other projects, they are too numerous to list. His achievements were great. Cao went to the United States three times for the affairs of the association, working diligently and tirelessly, and eventually became ill due to his hard work. In 1920, he returned to China from the United States. Because he was weak and unable to work hard, the doctor advised him to rest. Therefore, in December of that year, he resigned from his position as general secretary of the YMCA and went to Beiping for recuperation. The board of directors then invited Cao to serve as honorary general secretary. Whenever there were important projects, they still consulted him. Cao was calm, decisive, and full of a sense of responsibility. He did not discriminate in his service, such as assisting in the formation of the Youth Association, assisting the Hankou YMCA in building an association building for the summer conference, and purchasing the Zhujia Yan base. He worked hard without complaint and did not avoid difficulties. His assistance to neighboring associations in their work and the training of talents for the YMCA are even smaller matters. Cao passed away from illness in Shanghai on the night of February 23, 1927, at the age of 55.

China Aviation Corporation Ordered to Prepare for the Yunnan Air Route 123

Preparatory Expenses of 250,000 Yuan

Using the Latest Twin-Engine Aircraft

The China Aviation Corporation, in order to develop transportation and in response to the demands of all sectors, had planned to open the Yunnan air route. Now, it has been ordered to speed up preparations, and the preparatory expenses of 250,000 yuan have been approved. The details are as follows:

Request to Open and Two Test Flights: Yunnan is located in the remote west, where transportation is inconvenient, and there are many high mountains and steep ridges, like a paradise outside the world. The people of the area have collectively requested the central government to open an air route to facilitate transportation. The China Aviation Corporation sent aircraft to conduct two test flights last year, one departing from Chongqing and one departing from Guangdong. However, both were unsuccessful due to bad weather and the inability to use a single-engine aircraft freely. Moreover, the expenses were huge, so it was delayed indefinitely until now.

Preparatory Expenses of 50,000 Yuan Allocated: Now, due to the urgent need for transportation and the need for development, Long Yun, Chairman of the Yunnan Provincial Government, requested the central government to prepare for the project early, and it was approved. The China Aviation Corporation was instructed to prepare quickly. The Yunnan airport and radio, etc., are being actively prepared by the _ party. The preparatory expenses of 250,000 yuan have been approved and 50,000 yuan has already been allocated.

Using the Latest Twin-Engine Aircraft: According to Dai Enji, general manager of the company, although the weather on this route is bad and there are many high mountains and steep ridges, using a twin-engine aircraft should not be a problem. The route will run from Chongqing through Guizhou to Yunnan. It is now being actively planned and it is proposed to purchase the latest type of Locke aircraft. However, repairs are slightly difficult. In addition, it is also necessary to consider the seating and fuel consumption issues, which should be taken seriously. However, a decision can be made in the short term.

Fujian Aircraft Completed: The Douglas new Fujian aircraft has been completed and is scheduled for a test flight in two or three days. The Shanghai-Guangdong route will be resumed as scheduled according to the regulations. Only one aircraft will be used temporarily. There is also a Douglas aircraft and a repaired Sikorsky aircraft, which will temporarily join the Shanghai-Hankou route.

Retrial of Four Kidnappers 124

Witnesses Not Yet Fully Summoned

Four Bandits Detained Awaiting Further Trial

Jin Jiulin, the inspector of the special agency of the French Concession Police, etc., arrested more than a dozen kidnappers in Tianjin in July of last year, including Geng Huatang, Zheng Tangsheng, Shang Zhen, Liu Yimin, and Wu Shaoting, and transferred them to Shanghai. It was found that the criminals had previously kidnapped Huang Yuyi, the deputy director of the Zhongnan Bank, Chen Yanghe, the assistant manager of the Siming Bank, He Shaochu, the owner of the Xinsenji Construction Factory, Huang Baohua, a wealthy dye merchant, murdered a fellow gang member Xiao Shaoxing, and kidnapped Chen Zhuling and Liang Huiwu, both compradores of Jardine Matheson, in Tianjin, tearing up the tickets and burying the bodies to destroy the evidence. The police immediately telegraphed Tianjin to exhume the bodies of Chen and Liang. At the same time, the bandits were sent to the Second Special Court to be prosecuted for kidnapping. Later, the criminal Geng Huatang committed suicide in prison out of fear of punishment. Subsequently, Zheng, Shang, Liu, and Wu were sentenced to death for repeated kidnapping, and the rest were acquitted. Later, because Zheng, Shang, Liu, and Wu did not accept the original judgment, they submitted a request to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for review, and the case was sent back to the Second Special Court for retrial. Wang Gangxu, the chief judge of the Criminal Division, held several hearings for investigation, but all of them were postponed because the witnesses and victims could not be summoned to court. This has been reported in previous newspapers. This case was reopened for continuation of the trial by Judge Wang the day before yesterday. Of the witnesses and victims summoned, only Huang Yuyi, Chen Yanghe, and He Shaoting appeared in court. According to Huang and Chen, they could not remember because it had been a long time. However, He Shaoting said that when he was kidnapped, the second defendant, Shang Zhen, seemed to be at the scene. He was sitting in the car, on my right hand side. At first, Shang's face was thin, but now he is fatter. When questioned, Zheng Tangsheng categorically denied being at the scene of the kidnapping or sharing the money. Shang Zhen testified that he was at home in Chuzhou at that time. After his mother died, he became a monk at the Baoben Hall on Mount Putuo and did not know about the kidnapping. The two criminals, Liu Yimin and Wu Shaoting, also denied the kidnapping. The confessions of the criminals were the same as the previous two times. As a result, the court ruled that the trial would be adjourned to a later date because the witnesses summoned were not complete. The four criminals, Zheng, Shang, Liu, and Wu, were still remanded to the detention center.

The Location of the Incident is in the Chinese Territory

The First Court Can Approve the Transfer

Russian woman Mei Kaofu, 43 years old, recently opened a bar and dance hall at No. 366 Qiujiang Road, Zhabei. The business was thriving and coveted by a fellow Russian rogue, Navik. Between the 17th and 19th of this month, he repeatedly went to Mei's place, claiming that he had a girlfriend, Sasha and her husband (also Russian),

It was discovered that you specialize in selling dance girls for profit, and the Russian newspaper has already published this news. He said that if he informs the Chinese authorities, the Public Security Bureau must be ordered to send detectives to arrest you. According to the law, you should be sentenced to three years in prison and the bar will be closed. Sasha and her husband know the details and will testify in court once reported, so there is no way to deny it. After hearing this, Mei knew that his purpose was to threaten and defraud money. She pretended to be frightened and asked for a way to avoid the matter. Navik was overjoyed and said that there was a way to apply to the court, but he needed 500 yuan, 350 yuan to give to his girlfriend Sasha, and 150 yuan to the Russian newspaper to prevent it from publishing the story. As a result, Mei agreed to pay 100 yuan first and agreed to meet at the Jewish Hotel at No. 250 Bazi Road at 3 p.m. the day before yesterday. She secretly reported to the Hongkou Police Station and sent Russian detective Grobov to wait. She took the money to the hotel and handed it to Navik. His accomplice, the Russian woman Sasha, was subsequently arrested and taken to the police station separately for detention. The next morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Division of the First Court. Li Zhishan, the lawyer of the Public Works Department, gave a detailed account of the situation, and said that the victim lived in the Chinese territory, and the defendants had repeatedly contacted her there, but the location of the arrest was on Bazi Road. The Public Security Bureau requested a transfer. If there is an official letter, they agree. He presented the money to the court for inspection. When questioned, the two defendants gave evasive answers. Then, the victim, Russian woman Mei Kaofu, testified about what happened. An officer from the Public Security Bureau came to court, claiming that he did not bring the official letter because of the rush. Judge Xiao Xieyun ordered the two defendants to be remanded in custody separately, pending the official transfer letter.

Grabbing a Young Widow 127

Both Sides Had Bad Intentions

The Young Widow Fled First After Hearing the News

Pan Xia, a woman from Yancheng, 50 years old, lived in a thatched shed in the Xiaoyang Bridge area, west of Jiaotong Road, Zhabei. Her son, Cai Bang, had passed away, leaving behind a widowed daughter-in-law, Ye, only 19 years old, who worked in a yarn factory and earned 20 yuan a month. After her husband's death, Guan Ruqi, a well-known local man, coveted her youth and the 20 yuan she earned each month, so he often tried to seduce her. However, Ye thought that Guan's behavior was bad and glared at him, and secretly told her mother-in-law Xia not to allow Guan to enter the house. The mother's family of Pan Xia also had cousins, Xia Xiansheng and Xia Xianyou, who wanted to marry Ye. The day before yesterday, they held the "fifth seven" memorial service for Ye's late husband, inviting relatives to dinner. Unexpectedly, at about 8 p.m., the Xia family invited dozens of people to capture Ye, and Guan Ruqi also invited dozens of people to snatch Ye to be his wife. However, Ye had already heard the news, so she dug a hole next to the thatched shed and secretly escaped. For a time, the young widow's whereabouts were unknown. Guan suspected that Xia had snatched her, and Xia suspected that Guan had snatched her. They argued endlessly. The Tanziawan Police Station heard about it and sent police to arrest Guan Ruqi, Pan Xia, Xia Xiansheng, Xia Tao, and Tao Shaoqing, and sent them to the Xinzha Public Security Bureau. After questioning, the official learned the details. Because Pan Ye had not been brought to the court, he sent detective Fang Chaofu yesterday to investigate and summon Ye to the court. Ye testified that because there were many people that night, she escaped to a relative's house in Xiaoshadu to take refuge. The rest of her testimony was similar to the above. After verifying the confession, the official, considering that the case was related to the abduction of a woman, ordered that the six people, including Pan Ruqi, be sent to the Public Security Bureau for disposal.

Catholic Faithful, Elderly Mrs. Yu, Kidnapped 133

Kidnapped Suddenly on the Way to Mass

Yellow Taxi Driver Disappears Simultaneously

Yesterday morning at approximately 8:00 AM, elderly Mrs. Yu, matriarch of the wealthy Yu Baoshan family of Guangdong origin, residing at No. 60, west of the Jiangsu Higher Third Branch on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, was on her way to church for prayer in her private chartered car. Suddenly, three kidnappers jumped out, each wielding a handgun, and forced Mrs. Yu into a pre-arranged rented yellow taxi parked by the roadside, disappearing without a trace. The taxi was found at noon in the Gaolang Bridge area of Lan Road, but the driver, Cai Amao, was also kidnapped along with Mrs. Yu. As of late at night, neither had been released. The details are as follows:

Kidnappers Rent a Car: At around 7:15 AM yesterday morning, two uninvited customers suddenly appeared at the Baker Road branch of the well-known Yellow Taxi Company in the city. One wore a dark green silk shirt and a melon-shaped hat, while the other, in a gray long gown, followed behind. They stated that they wanted to rent a car to be taken to the Shanjiayuan area near the North Mud City Bridge. As they spoke, they took out a silver dollar from their person and gave it to the branch's accountant, who dispatched Cai Amao (age 36, from Tongzhou), the driver of rental permit No. 12032, to drive them. The two men boarded the car one after the other and drove straight away.

Mrs. Yu's Faith: No. 60, west of the Jiangsu Higher Third Branch on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, is the mansion of Yu Mishantang, a wealthy Guangdong merchant. Inside resides the mistress of the house, elderly Mrs. Yu, who, although over sixty years old, is energetic and devoutly Catholic. Every Sunday and holiday, she attends Mass at church without fail. She is known for her frugality, and only uses a chartered car (Municipal Permit No. 3757, Concession No. 80) when going out.

Kidnapped into the Car: Yesterday was Sunday. Mrs. Yu got up at 7:00 AM, washed, and after a quick breakfast, it was already 8:00 AM. She promptly boarded her chartered car. The driver, Lu Huixiang, pulled the car eastward. Just as they reached the entrance of No. 5, west of the Jiangsu Higher Third Branch, three kidnappers suddenly rushed out, each drawing a handgun, ordering the driver to stop the car. At the same time, two kidnappers forced Mrs. Yu into a pre-arranged yellow taxi parked by the roadside, and sped eastward. The license plate number of the taxi was No. 12032, the same one rented from Baker Road earlier.

Police Pursuit: The chartered car driver, Lu Huixiang, was stunned and frightened when he witnessed the kidnapping of his employer. After a long while, he regained his composure and hurriedly drove the empty car back home to report the incident. The family then reported it to the Loujiawan Police Station in charge. The head detective then dispatched a large number of Chinese and foreign detectives in all directions, but they were nowhere to be found. The head detective urgently notified the Public Concession and the Public Security Bureau's various sub-bureaus by telephone to intercept the vehicle, but to no avail. It wasn't until noon that the taxi was found near Gaolang Bridge on Lan Road, but it was empty. The driver, Cai Amao, was also missing at the same time.

Speculation: After the incident, police detectives speculated that when the two kidnappers rented the car, they said they only wanted to go to the North Mud City Bridge. At that time, Cai Amao must have driven to a place near where they said, and then lured Cai into the kidnappers' lair, where he was kept under surveillance. Then, a kidnapper who was a skilled driver drove the car to Avenue Edward VII to wait for the ransom target. Otherwise, if Cai were also in the car at the same time, he would have been pushed out of the car midway, and would not have been kidnapped as well. Others speculated that Mrs. Yu's kidnapping may involve some kind of issue, but this may be overthinking it.

Five Years Ago: The reporter distinctly remembers that five years ago, the mistress of the Yu Mansion at No. 43 Rue Courbet, also a Catholic, was kidnapped in front of the church on Rue de l'Eglise in the French Concession while attending Mass. She was later ransomed with a large sum of money. This time, the kidnapped person is also a woman, also surnamed Yu, and also kidnapped while attending Catholic Mass. The kidnapping location is also in the French Concession. This is truly a rare coincidence, a sight to behold. However, according to general opinion, the Mrs. Yu kidnapped five years ago is the same Mrs. Yu kidnapped today. But when the reporter inquired at the Yu residence on Rue Courbet, they absolutely denied that the two were the same person.

Passed the Constitution and Work Program

Yan Zhenyu and Others Elected as Directors

The Shanghai Women's Progressive Association, since its preparation, has reached more than a month. Yesterday, the inaugural meeting was held at Wuben Girls' High School, where the constitution was passed and directors were elected. The details are as follows:

Elected Directors: The elected directors include Wu Zaiyi, Yan Zhenyu, Cai Jinying, Jin Guangmei, Qiu Xisheng, Tang Naixin, Tan Shuliang, Zhu Shangquan, Fan Zhiping, Jiang Huiruo, Chen Yongsheng, Ling Qinru, Yang Zhihao, etc., a total of thirteen people. Ships Passing Through the Port of Newchwang Should Reduce Speed 136

Hydrographic Bureau Notifies the Shipping Industry

Various ships in the Liaodong Bay Newchwang port area on the northern coast often cause accidents due to excessive speed while navigating in the port. In order to reduce the risk of accidents, the Hydrographic Bureau yesterday issued a notice to the shipping industry, informing them to reduce speed. The location is in the Newchwang port area, approximately 122 degrees 16 minutes east longitude and approximately 40 degrees 41 minutes north latitude.

New Construction on Avenue Joffre 137

A new market has been built east of the Paris Theatre on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession. The market is conveniently located with easy access. It contains 21 shops and 10 new-style residences. The building has a novel design and is well-equipped, with ample light and good ventilation. There is a fountain in the market and two gardens on the side, full of seasonal flowers and trees, which adds to its elegance. Except for two or three shops that are still being negotiated, all 21 shops have been rented out, and most have already moved in and started business. The business of each shop is extremely busy, making it a good place to do business. Facing Avenue Joffre, there is also a brand-new six-story building with five shops and fifteen residences. It is fully equipped with hot and cold water pipes, radiators ("hot air pipes"), electric stoves, bathrooms, and sanitary appliances. The rent is also very cheap. Those interested are advised to make inquiries early to avoid missing out on a good opportunity. Contact the Avenue Joffre Market Office next to the Paris Theatre on Avenue Joffre and Rue Voyron.

The Telegram Bureau Will Translate Cables Starting Next Month 138

Those Who Need Translation Should Notify the Telegram Bureau by Letter

The Shanghai Telegram Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, following the ministry's order, will uniformly translate all Chinese coded telegrams into text starting from November 1st of this year before sending them to benefit the public. However, considering the psychology of the business community in this city, who often wish to translate telegrams themselves to prevent leakage, the bureau, in order to respect the wishes of the recipients and avoid delays caused by the translation process, has stipulated that starting from November 1st, for Chinese coded telegrams sent to recipients in various places, those who require the bureau to translate them must officially submit a letter before 5:00 PM on the 25th of this month, affixing the seal of the letter, directly to the bureau for handling. Those who do not wish to have them translated do not need to send a letter. The bureau will deliver the telegram in code as usual for convenience.

Public Concession Bus Company Issues Monthly Season Tickets 139

School Tickets Will Be Discontinued at the End of the Month

The British-owned China General Omnibus Company announced that starting from November 1934, it will issue monthly season tickets for adults at ten dollars per ticket and for schoolchildren under the age of seventeen at six dollars per ticket per month. The school tickets already issued by the company will no longer be issued after October 31st. Those who wish to purchase monthly season tickets must come in person to the company's office at No. 111 Sassoon House on the Bund of Nanjing Road. The company will start selling tickets on the 26th of this month.

Wang Shuhuai Accompanies Son to Shanghai for Medical Treatment and Goes Missing 142

It Was Only Learned Yesterday That He Was Detained by the Public Security Bureau

The Xianju Fellow-Townsmen Association Requests His Release

The Shanghai Xianju Fellow-Townsmen Association states that according to fellow-townsman Wang Huanhui, his father, Wang Shuhuai, accompanied his son to Shanghai for medical treatment and went missing. He had posted advertisements in newspapers to find him. Recently, he learned that his father was detained by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. He requests a certificate for bail. Yesterday, the association sent a letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau requesting that bail be granted. The original text is as follows: "Submitting a request for a fellow-townsman to be bailed out from unjust detention. According to a letter from fellow-townsman Wang Huanhui, his father, Shuhuai, accompanied him to Shanghai for medical treatment on the 7th of this month. He has been missing since he went out on Double Tenth Day. He has inquired with relatives and friends, but has not been able to find him. He was extremely anxious and had already reported it to the Baoshan Road Public Security Sub-bureau and posted advertisements in newspapers to find him. It was only yesterday that news came that he was being detained by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. His father is an honest villager and would never have any transgressive behavior. He is in prison, and it is not known what crime he committed. We are requesting your esteemed bureau to quickly rescue him to redress his grievances." At the same time, according to a letter from Zhang Fengsu, her husband, Zheng Songnan, was also innocently detained by the Municipal Public Security Bureau (the rest is the same as the previous letter, so it is omitted). It has come to light that Wang Shuhuai is an honest elder in our hometown and would never have any misconduct. Zheng Songnan is also an honest businessman, and they are both innocent and implicated in the case. Their situation is very pitiful. We have prepared this document to request your approval to grant them bail to avoid their grievances. It would be a great act of kindness."

A Young Woman Commits Suicide After a Quarrel with Her Husband 143

Du Lan, a 24-year-old woman from Wuxi and the younger sister of Du Aisheng, who drives a car for a real estate company, residing at No. 500 Sande Fang, Rue Lupan in the French Concession, was introduced to Zhao Nai, a postman from Nanxiang who works at the express mail section No. 80 of the Post Office at No. 5 Chongxiao Lane, Caojia Temple in the Old West Gate, in February of this year. However, after the marriage, there were often quarrels between the couple. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, at around 3:00 PM, Du Lan suddenly had thoughts of ending her life. Taking advantage of her husband's absence, she swallowed raw opium in an attempt to commit suicide. At around 5:00 PM, she was discovered by a neighbor and sent to Shanghai Hospital by her aunt for emergency treatment. After examination by the hospital doctor, it was found that she had taken too much poison and could not be saved. She died at around midnight. Afterwards, the deceased's brother learned of the incident and reported it to Tang Jing, the chief of the Wenmiao Road Police Station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau in charge. The police chief immediately sent police officers to the station to interrogate Zhao Nai. At the same time, he asked the local headman to request an inspection from the local court. The court appointed Prosecutor Zhao Chuanjia to go to the scene with the coroner at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon for an inspection. It was confirmed that she had died from poisoning, and it was ordered that the body be placed in a coffin, it was said.

Fire on Songxue Street 144

Bao Yinsheng, a native of Changzhou, lives at No. 2, Lane 1, Rongxiang Lane, Songxue Street, Fangbang Road, inside the Old North Gate, and acts as the second landlord. The house is a three-story stone-gate house, with two tenants, including the Dexingxiang grocery store, renting the downstairs east wing, and three tenants renting the upstairs, totaling six families in one house, which is very complicated. At around 4:30 AM yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the woodpile in the loft of the kitchen, quickly piercing the roof, with flames soaring into the sky. Fortunately, the police officer on duty at the Old North Gate Police Station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau in charge discovered it and immediately notified the fire brigades of various districts, who quickly drove fire trucks to the scene. After the firefighters worked hard to extinguish the fire, it was extinguished at around 6:00 AM. Only one kitchen was burned down. At that time, the general neighbors were awakened from their sleep and fled in panic, causing chaos. Chief Shen Zhenhua led the police officers to the scene to suppress the situation, maintain order, and investigate the cause of the fire. Bao Yinsheng, who started the fire, was taken to the station for interrogation, it was said.

Carelessness at the Feihua Inn 145

Losses Exceeding Ten Thousand Dollars

The Hu Shouji Feihua Inn at No. 427, No. 4 Bridge, Zhongshan Road, Zhabei, which is run by Hu Shushun from Changzhou, suddenly caught fire at 6:45 PM last night. The flying flowers (fireworks) inside the inn immediately ignited, and the flames soared. The Zhabei Fire Brigade No. 1, 2, and 3 then rushed to the scene to help extinguish the fire. It was not until 9:30 PM that the fire was extinguished. Because the inn was full of flying flowers, once they caught fire, they could not be put out. As a result, all six of the inn's single-story houses were reduced to ashes. The loss of goods and property is estimated to be more than ten thousand dollars. It is said that the fire insurance covers only four or five thousand taels.

Yu Baisheng, a local, 28 years old, a plasterer, residing at No. 491, Huanlong Road, fell from the third floor of No. 167, Avenue Ghisi yesterday at noon due to carelessness. He broke his right leg and left arm on the spot, and also suffered internal injuries, which were very serious. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, he was repairing a leak on the roof of the De'an Clock Factory at No. 41, Lane 1017, Tangshan Road, Hongkou. He fell to the ground and broke his skull, losing consciousness. He was taken to Tongren Hospital by car, but died at around 7:00 PM after treatment proved ineffective.

Adopting a Son Only to Have His Daughter and Widowed Daughter-in-Law Flee Together 147

Enjoying Happiness with One Stone Killing Two Birds

Extreme Joy Turns to Sorrow, Captured in Beijing

The Wu Changchun paper store at No. 172 Wanyu Street, Dongjiadu, outside the Small South Gate in this city, is run by Wu Genxian from Jiangxi. Wu once married and had a son and a daughter. The eldest daughter's name is Wu Qiulan, and the younger son's name is Wu Guozhu. He married Wang Aiyu, a woman from the same hometown, in the first month of the lunar calendar in 1929. The young couple had a very harmonious relationship. However, both of their two grandsons died one after another. Guozhu assisted his father in managing the store and was unhappy. Unexpectedly, on the 19th day of the first month of the lunar calendar last year, Guozhu died of illness. His father, Wu Changchun, thought that it was not a long-term solution to leave behind a young widow with no descendants. He discussed it with his wife and widowed daughter-in-law and agreed to adopt Yuan Yinzhu from Henan as an adopted son, who then served as Wang Aiyu's husband after entering the family. Wang Yinzhu also worked in the paper store. Yuan paid his adoptive father Genxian eighty yuan as a gift at the time. However, not long after, Wu Genxian disliked his adopted son and changed him to a partner, planning to remarry his widowed daughter-in-law to Pudong. Because the plan was not kept secret, Yuan and his daughter-in-law learned of it. On September 12th of this year, they took all their jewelry, clothes, and belongings, along with his eldest daughter, Wu Qiulan, and fled home to Nanjing to live. After Wu Genxian's widowed daughter-in-law, Wang Aiyu, his eldest daughter, Wu Qiulan, and Yuan Yinzhu suddenly disappeared, he immediately reported to Yi Zuanren, the chief of the first precinct and first station (now Dongjiadu Police Station) of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, accusing Yuan Yinzhu of seducing his widowed daughter-in-law and eldest daughter and instigating them to flee. He attached a list of missing items and photos of the three people, requesting that they be investigated and arrested. Chief Yi sent officers to investigate once and forwarded the report to Bureau Chief Wen Hong'en, who sent letters to various places for investigation. It is now known that the three men and women, including Wang Aiyu, have been captured by the Capital Police Station in Beijing. Bureau Chief Wen has ordered the Detective Captain Yu Ying of the bureau to send Detective Leader Wu Xiufeng and Detective Gui Guofang to Beijing yesterday to bring back the three people, including Wang, along with two suitcases. They have been handed over to the Third Section for handling.

Zhuang Songfu, Chen Gongqia, and 22 others initiated the seventieth birthday celebration for Madam Lai, the mother of Bao, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Garden. On that day, the weather was sunny and the wind was gentle, and all the wise men were present. They all personally congratulated the birthday altar. Mother Bao's sons, Bodu, Yiren, Shuliang, and Bizhong, returned the courtesy as required. The guests toasted and drank until midnight, and the celebration was a complete success. It can be called grand. Mother Bao, deeply grateful for the kindness of the heads of various Yuan, ministries, bureaus, officers, colleagues, and friends, as well as the great ceremony, has ordered Bodu to keep them properly, to be used for establishing a primary school to benefit poor children, and to repay the kindness of the heads of various agencies, colleagues, relatives, and friends.

Cracking Down on a Lottery Parlor with Listening Devices in Xujiahui 149

Since taking office, Hong Zhen, chief of the Xujiahui Police Station in West Shanghai, has been very strict in cracking down on gambling. Therefore, more than a dozen cases have been seized and sent for investigation. Recently, it was discovered that Zhang Xialiang, a Ningbo native residing at No. 1856 Rue Hearne, had privately set up a lottery parlor with listening devices in his home to provide gambling for people. Three suspects, the ringleader of the lottery parlor, Lu Xiaodi, a local, Zhang Xialiang, a Ningbo native, and Cai Zhenhua, a Chaozhou native, were arrested on the spot. Lu Xiaodi and others confessed to privately setting up a lottery parlor with listening devices and accepting gambling funds. Recent News from the Civilian Sanatorium 151

The Civilian Sanatorium at the intersection of Weihaiwei Road and Chongqing Road was founded by medical doctors Wang Peiyuan and Yang Zhongfu. It has magnificent buildings, a large scale, and serves the society with outstanding achievements. It is the only civilian sanatorium in the city. Yang Zhongfu, the director of the hospital, has always been enthusiastic about social undertakings. Recently, he has personally been hospitalized for diagnosis and treatment out of concern for the suffering of the common people, and his spirit of service is greatly admired. It has recently been learned that, in view of the increasing harm of opium and the fact that many Chinese people are anesthetized by it, the hospital has set up a separate smoking cessation department in addition to various other departments. In order to reduce the back-and-forth travel for those who want to quit, dozens of exquisitely decorated wards have been set up to help those who are determined to get rid of their bad habits within a limited number of days. Both residential and outpatient smoking cessation services are available. The fees are low, the care is comprehensive, and the number of people coming to quit smoking is endless. It is said that the hospital is having difficulty coping with the demand.

Publishing Circle 154

"Modern Couples": Elegant in Both Prose and Sentiment. The recently published book "Modern Couples" is written by Shenbao reporter Huang Jiping. The content clarifies various issues concerning love and marriage between the sexes, emphasizing the importance of carefully examining each other's personality, academic achievements, and everything else before marriage. After marriage, it emphasizes the importance of mutual affection, love, and understanding between husband and wife. The characters in the book have modern and appropriate ideas, with gentle and considerate wording, intertwined emotions, and sincere words. The book, over 200,000 words long, is divided into four stages: acquaintance, engagement, marriage, and family life. The plot is winding and vivid. Originally the author's own account, it is exceptionally colorful when written with her flowery prose. Liu Yazi, Zhang Henshui, Zhou Shoujuan, and others have written prefaces praising the book, considering it excellent reading material for modern young men and women. It is reported that the book is currently sold by Shanghai Life Bookstore, Modern Bookstore, Shenbao Service Department, Dazhong Bookstore, Author Bookstore, Xinhua Bookstore. The paperback is priced at 7 jiao 5 fen per copy, and the hardcover is 9 jiao 5 fen.

Free Talk

Re-establishing 159

— Zhang Weile

Since the blue-eyed, blonde-haired, colorless race stepped into the ancient Eastern country with their warships and cargo, the power of cannons can certainly make you bow your head, and the flaunting of so-called material civilization will also make you succumb. As such, as long as they are blue-eyed and blonde-haired, you will be respectfully awed! As long as something comes from the homeland of the blue-eyed and blonde-haired, it is a priceless treasure! Alas! The people of the ancient Eastern country have lost their self-confidence!

I think that the unreasonable arrogance of the blue-eyed and blonde-haired does indeed make us feel extremely indignant, but our own lack of self-confidence is our fatal flaw! We will not concern ourselves with the coolies with low levels of knowledge who want to earn a few more dollars to maintain their livelihoods; what is most regrettable is that intellectuals and so-called upper-class people are also unable to extricate themselves, unable to find their own beliefs. Every move, if there is no precedent in the homeland of the blue-eyed and blonde-haired, is like an illegitimate child who has not been publicly recognized, and is deeply felt to be base and contemptible! As long as it is something that the homeland of the blue-eyed and blonde-haired "already has," there is no question of nobility or baseness, and it is okay to follow suit!

I am rambling too much; let me give two examples:

The so-called circus that is now popular, I think is about the same as the tricks we have always seen on the streets! However, in the past, the more noble people would not deign to look at any tricks, but now the circus has tickets costing three or four dollars each, yet carriages are like dragons and the gate is like a market. Although the circus is nothing more than some trick-playing acts, because it comes from the homeland of the blue-eyed and blonde-haired, its value suddenly increases a hundredfold.

Here is another example: the university students of our highest institutions of learning are knowledgeable enough, right? In the past, we all lived in some schools, and there were also cases of older students bullying new students, but this was an unconscious act by a few students with low-level interests, and most students who had a little self-respect would not bother to participate. Now it is different, because this kind of behavior has recently been confirmed to exist in the homeland of the blue-eyed and blonde-haired, where the term "dragging corpses" already exists. Thus, they drag and drag especially hard, dragging it until the news in the newspapers is full of reports, and this is enough to satisfy them! I believe that if they had not obtained the confirmation of the civilization of the blue-eyed and blonde-haired, they would not be so enthusiastic!

We should respectfully accept the essence of culture and civilization, but we must eliminate the dross of civilization. We can hardly avoid being indignant at the arrogance of the blue-eyed and blonde-haired, but we must maintain our self-confidence. If we blindly follow and blindly praise, I am afraid that we will never be able to escape the status of slaves in spirit, and we can only let the blue-eyed and blonde-haired people stride ahead forever!

The Past 160

— Zhou Wen

The sun sets below the horizon, and the electric lights come on in the room. Ah, a yawn, and the day is over. Even if you have been sweating shirtless in the sun during the day, or wracking your brains at your desk with your sleeves rolled up, it all disappears as quickly as the sun, and is past. What remains is only the fatigue after a day of labor, etched on the face that is etched with wrinkles.

Although this "past" is past in time, from the perspective of the entire society, the accumulation of all energy is constantly increasing. Through the elimination and refining of time, from barbarism to civilization, from today to tomorrow, a continuous radiance shines in front of the continuous trajectory. This is development, evolution. The wheel of history, on this black earth, has carried a hope that is clearer day by day from the door of the past.

Believing in the hope, standing on the platform of the "present" to observe the "past," throwing all those chunks of experience into the engine of the wheel, then the sound emitted by this "past" will become an ode to tomorrow, rather than a meaningless sigh.

However, man is ultimately the "spirit" of all things. Whenever he encounters a setback, he will hug his knees and sit on the head of the bed, looking at the gray and dim corner, or stand with his hands behind his back under the moonlight, gazing at the distant reaches where the stars are twinkling. Then "inspiration" comes, and the game of hide-and-seek under the flower shade in childhood, or even the slap in the face from his father for playing hide-and-seek, become beautiful pictures worthy of tracing in his eyes, deeply savoring those remnants that can never be returned. But he insists on deeply savoring them, and then sighs with a frown. He drinks from a large bowl, smokes heavily, and the next day you can see his pale and gloomy face. In the blink of an eye, he is hunchbacked, his beard is disheveled, and he walks towards his grave step by step.

Gorky, in his works, repeatedly makes clear criticisms of these facts. In "Creatures That Once Were Men," he says: "There are often many people in the world who, by recalling the past, cause all the abilities of the present and all the hopes of the future to disappear." In "Chelkash" he also says: "Memory is the spur of the disappointed, it can give life to the stones of the past, pour honey into the poison drunk in the old days, make a person realize his wrongdoings, make him love the past, and deprive him of hope for the future."

"The past," for an individual, should be thrown away like a rotten apple by the side of your road, and you should not look back.

Farewell (Part 1) 161

— Cao Ming

In the spring of the year I was fifteen, when people were beginning to work hard for silkworms, an elderly uncle from a distant family fell ill, and my eldest aunt ran back to my house. With my mother's consent, she took me back to her small house to help her manage the household affairs.

I didn't know much about my eldest aunt and uncle in detail, but one thing I was very clear about: they had always lived in quarrels. Whenever they met, they would quarrel. When they were apart, they worked hard. Comfortable laughter could never be found between them. I often wondered, what force would bind them together to live for decades?

My aunt was completely a heartless fellow. In the twenty-odd days I lived there, she never stopped cursing him. It was as if she didn't even have a shred of pity.

It was on the night my uncle died that I understood my uncle and aunt. After that, the shadows of the two of them often appeared in my mind.

"You should still get up."

I, who was sleeping on the bamboo kang wrapped in a quilt, was ordered. Following a low and resolute voice, "It's almost over."

I struggled to open my eyes, searching for the small kerosene lamp in the dark house. It was guiding my aunt, who had half of her hair gone and was a little hunched over, as she groped around the house.

The slow groans of the seriously ill and the rustling sound of silkworm larvae eating occupied this surrounding area that seemed to be the boundary between humans and ghosts.

In the corner of the room, under the shrine, my short uncle was lying on two thin wooden boards. His originally round face looked as if someone had dug out all the muscles; a pair of sunken, dull eyes, matched with a nose that only had two holes left and a mouth whose upper lip had already shrunk, and the windpipe was like a broken pump, with air entering and exiting with difficulty. And, clearly, he exhaled for twice as long as he inhaled. My aunt stood in front of the bed, holding a lamp, and said with her often watery eyes, "It's almost over." Then she pulled the cotton quilt, which was as dark as the sky, toward my uncle's neck. "You keep an eye out for a while. I'm going to feed the silkworms."

I pretended not to hear her instructions, jumped and hid behind her, holding tightly to a corner of her clothes. This rash action gave my aunt a chance to vent her frustration.

"Useless fellow, I was already married when I was as old as you. What are you afraid of? People are going to die eventually." She said in a rough voice, probably afraid of offending me, so she explained to me again, "You need to know, the land has always been the same size from ancient times to the present. If no one died, then, think about it, wouldn't people have to fight for places to live? And there's another thing: the money in the world is also limited. So—" She grabbed a handful of chopped mulberry leaves and carefully placed them in the silkworm nest (note). "So, people are cruel things. They abandon or even harm their own kind for money. Don't you see? The richer people are, the more cruel they are. Then, think about it, what kind of world is this? How can someone as timid as you avoid being bullied?"

She lowered her head very low, gently stroking the silkworm nests with great force, sometimes even putting her ear on the basket, as if whispering to them, serving one nest after another. Her attitude of being so careful with the silkworms when someone so close was about to die made me very strange and angry.

Usually, my uncle would say to her in such a tone:

"Where have I let you down? I always do things first. A seventy-year-old man still runs up to the mulberry dikes to water them every day... Where have I let you down, except for being poor?" My uncle, who was a head shorter than my aunt, would always bend over from his back to his head, and continued this posture for a long time.

When she heard "Why don't you drink your wine?" or "The silkworm moths are calling you," my aunt would speak in a less rough voice, but her expression would become even more depressed. If she drank a little too much wine, she would start cursing incessantly like a madwoman, until my uncle picked up the water jug or mulberry basket and went out, and then she would give a meaningless, silly laugh and sing her wedding song to me:

"Olives are green and tender and ready to be picked, alas, what is it that my parents didn't care about their young daughter suffering so much? I became a daughter-in-law when I was fifteen, alas,

………………

………………"

Then, she would excitedly make gestures and tell how on the first night of her marriage, she pushed my uncle to the ground with one hand, and later, his docile, sheep-like, unresisting attitude annoyed her so much that she couldn't sleep all night. From the next day on, she began to scold him.

"I've been scolding him from the time he was twenty-nine until now, when he's almost seventy. That poor, stupid pig!" she said very regretfully.

Note: Made of bamboo strips woven into a circle, like a tabletop, with raised edges around it, commonly called a nest basket. Silkworm farmers often use them to raise silkworms and is simply called a silkworm nest.

Foreign Dusk 162

— Tang Kai

I sit on the stool by the window, staring blankly at the sky, ah! This foreign dusk stirs up endless melancholy in me. I fantasize that my life is just like the faint glow of the setting sun, which has been defeated by the god of night. Even if I muster all my courage again, I still cannot break through this layer of obscurity. My lost youth has no possibility of lingering. I once carried a piece of fervent hope before I started wandering, but now! All hopes have turned into bubbles! Slowly, like withered roses, there is no time to flourish again, and even like the firm ice accumulated on the mountain peaks for decades, waiting to melt, alas! The belt of life tightly ties my body and mind. I have sold my labor at a meager price! Freedom! My blood is still boiling, but reality has triumphed over all hopes. Is there a glimmer of light? Far away, a cry of "Paris-Soir" awakens me from my confusion. I stand up and face the round mirror on the table. I see two hot tears streaming down my haggard face.

Written in the hospital on September 6, 1934

Near Paris

Little Westward Boy (3) 163

— Written by Langston Hughes, Translated by Fulan

Christmas arrived, and Cindy sent a large box of drugstore candies to her mother in Darside. He initially wanted to spend fifteen cents on a pair of long, cyan earrings for Grandma Hager, but he feared she wouldn't like them, so he bought her white handkerchiefs. He also sent a beautiful card to Black Reed, his aunt, because one snowy October day, his aunt saw him sweeping the reception room from outside the window, and she called him outside to talk to her. She put a small slip of paper with her new address on it in his hand.

"Matelee has moved to Kansas City," she said, "so I no longer live there. Keep this address safe, so you know where I am whenever Mama needs me."

Then she left in the snow, looking beautiful in her cheap leather coat, black high-heeled shoes, and cyan stockings. Cindy had often seen her passing the hotel entrance with different men, sometimes with the owner of the Cashman Casino, or Billy Sanderly, but almost always with vulgar-looking men wearing round felt hats and gold teeth. Cindy remembered that she didn't tell him the street number of her new house. He put the piece of paper in his pocket and went back to sweeping. Yes, he was happy to see his aunt, Black Reed.

One Saturday afternoon, several white men sat in the reception room smoking and reading newspapers. Cindy wiped the chairs, dusted them, and then took the spittoons to clean. This work didn't require much attention, and he could use a soft cloth to wipe them. He could let his mind think of other things. He thought of Black Reed, then of school and what he should do when he grew up; he thought of Hailey May, the little girl next door who had gotten a job washing dishes for white people; he thought of Jamie Lynn, the little boy next door who had no mother; Cindy also wondered what his parents were doing in another city, or if they needed him to be with them. He also thought about how old and frail Grandma Hager had become, with her white hair, how she was now panting over the laundry tub but never complaining; how she waited for him every Saturday, leaving the kitchen stove fire on so he could warm up after walking such a long way in the cold, and how she hoped he would one day become a great man... Sitting in the back room of this hotel, Cindy often wondered how people could become great. At that time, he made the spittoons shiny and beautiful. He often thought about how people could be great.

Tonight, he had to pick up newspapers in the reception room, run errands for the head waiter, and shine shoes. He would have to work very late. After he put away the spittoons, he fixed himself a small meat sandwich and a cup of coffee for dinner, and then he would go back to help Charlie, if he could... Charlie was really a good old boy. He had given Cindy one dollar just for doing his job, and often helped him with small accounts, let Cindy go to the telegraph office, or do some other small improper things for the guests upstairs... Really, Charlie was a kind and interesting person.
