The Chinese Art Education Society Held Its Inaugural Meeting Yesterday 167

More Than One Hundred Members Attended, Director Pan Personally Delivered Instructions

Ma Gongyu, Yan Kechang, and Eleven Others Elected as Directors

The Chinese Art Education Society held its inaugural meeting at the junior high school department of Shanghai High School on Shangwen Road at 10:00 AM yesterday. The opening ceremony was in the morning, and discussions on proposals and the election of officers were in the afternoon. Details are recorded as follows:

Attending Members: Including Ma Gongyu, Yan Kechang, Song Banggan, Xu Zexiang, Zhang Chenbo, Yu Jifan, Jiang Danshu, Ni Yide, Fu Boliang, Zhao Weizu, Wu Mengfei, Ji Xiaobo, Tang Jun, Zhu Zhiwei, Mo Yunxuan, Wang Yuanbo, Teng Gu, Xie Gongzhan, and more than one hundred and forty others. Wang Longzhang from the Municipal Party Department and Nie Haifan from the Municipal Education Bureau attended for guidance. Director Pan Gongzhan of the Municipal Education Bureau, as well as Wang Jiyuan and Wang Yachen, also attended and gave speeches.

Meeting Situation: The meeting started at nine o'clock, with Ma Gongyu, Yan Kechang, and Wang Yungong as the presidium, Zhu Zhiwei as the master of ceremonies, and Liu Shuxun as the recorder. After the formalities, Chairman Ma Gongyu delivered the opening speech, followed by Yan Kechang's report on the preparatory process. Then, Director Pan of the Municipal Education Bureau, Wang Longzhang of the Municipal Party Department, and Wang Jiyuan and Wang Yachen gave speeches. No photos were taken. Lunch was served. The meeting continued at 2:00 PM to discuss the charter and proposals and to elect officers. The meeting adjourned at around five o'clock.

Director's Instructions: Director Shen of the Municipal Education Bureau said in his instructions, "I am very honored to attend the inaugural meeting of your society today. The decline of China's inherent art cannot be reversed without everyone's efforts. Art encompasses all aspects of life, such as clothing, food, shelter, and transportation, and should all be artistic. We should make the artistic elements universal so that everyone can know the importance of art and life and apply it to their lives. How to promote artistic life to the general public and move away from art being detached from life and becoming the aristocracy of art, appreciated by noble people? Therefore, this point should be promoted so that the general public can obtain a good life."

Discussion of Proposals: The meeting continued at 2:00 PM, chaired by Yan Kechang. Wang Longzhang of the Municipal Party Department and Ding Nianxian of the Municipal Education Bureau attended for guidance. The charter was first discussed, amended, and passed, followed by discussions on proposals, including (1) requesting the Ministry of Education to establish art museums in major cities of each province; (2) requesting the Ministry of Education and provincial education departments to organize art education committees; (3) requesting the Ministry of Education to issue a notice to all primary and secondary schools nationwide to strictly follow the curriculum standards for labor education; (4) requesting the Ministry of Education to hold the second National Art Exhibition; (5) requesting the Ministry of Education to change art colleges into academy systems; (6) requesting the Municipal Education Bureau to organize a music broadcasting inspection committee; (7) requesting the Palace Museum Management Committee to allow members of this society to participate in the art objects of the Palace Museum; (8) establishing practical art night schools and art normal schools; (9) establishing art research institutes and art consulting offices, totaling sixteen proposals, which were resolved to be submitted to the board of directors for discussion.

Election of Directors: Ma Gongyu, Yan Kechang, Fu Boliang, Wang Yungong, Shi Chongpeng, Zhu Yuansong, Shi Wenbin, Zhang Meisun, Zhu Zhiwei, and Shen Xunlou were elected as directors. Ding Nianxian, Wang Longzhang, Chen Songchun, Jiang Danshu, and Yu Jifan were elected as supervisors.

The Editorial and Review Committee of the Ministry of Interior Held a Discussion Meeting with Book Publishers Yesterday 168

More Than Sixty Representatives From Commercial Press, China Bookstore, and Others Attended

Requesting the Abolition of Sending Books to the Ministry for Review

The Editorial and Review Committee of the Ministry of Interior held a discussion meeting with all book publishers in Shanghai at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce on the third floor at 2:00 PM yesterday. Details are recorded as follows:

Attending Representatives: In addition to Pan Jidong, a member of the Editorial and Review Committee, attendees included Zhong Jiyu from World Publishing House, Ding Jingxin from Liming Bookstore, Lin Zhongliang from Xinzhi Bookstore, Wang Maolin from Xiangxing Art Society, Ru Hanyang from Nanqiang Bookstore, Chen Zhenhua from Xin Shengming Bookstore, Li Yaotang from Middle School Student Bookstore, Wang Jiecun from Modern Bookstore, Ji Zhizhong from New China Bookstore, Huang Zhaoping from Medical Bookstore, Hu Junsheng from Youxin Bookstore, Xu Baozhi from Shanggu Shufang, Zhang Shuliang from Commercial Press, Xie Jiasong from Shen Bao Special Distribution Department, Zhang Guangzong from Qinfen Bookstore, Li Zhiyun from Beixin Bookstore, Lufei Bohong from China Bookstore (represented by Wu Gusheng), and Shen Junsheng from Datong Bookstore, totaling more than sixty people.

Discussion Situation: Chairman Pan Jidong first expressed his views on (1) the opinions on sending books for review in the detailed rules for the implementation of the Publication Law; (2) the announcement of the national book statistics; (3) published books should be sent to the Ministry within three months in accordance with the Publication Law, and new books should be sent to the Ministry within three months after publication; (4) the publication date of publications should be in the Gregorian calendar. After discussion by the majority of attendees, it was considered that the book review in the detailed rules for implementation was greatly detrimental to publication and culture, and a joint request was made to Reviewer Pan to convey it to the Ministry of Interior for abolition. The meeting adjourned at four o'clock.

The Dispute at Luoyang School 174

Luodian County Luoyang Elementary School has been established for many years and has achieved excellent results. In addition to commuting students, there are also 19 boarders. This summer, Zhu Xin took over as principal not long ago, and there was a rampant act of teachers beating elementary school students. On the evening of the 9th, Zhao Zhengqin, an educator at the school, instructed the cook to prepare several dishes for use. At dinner time, the educators were all drinking outside. When they returned to the school late at night, they were all drunk. Suddenly, they found that the dishes had not been prepared, suspected that the boarding students had stolen the food, and then used their drunkenness to interrogate the boarding students one by one. The students' cries reached the outdoors. Afterwards, the students' families questioned the school, and although they were relieved in many ways, no incidents occurred, but a majority of them had withdrawn from school.

Special Article

Answering Mr. Liu Yizheng on "Wonderful Trick to Protect the Nose" (2) Zhu Yixin 175

The troops continued to advance, and when they arrived at a place, many farmers were building walls by the fields. The officer asked them, "What are you building walls for?" The farmers replied, "The seedlings in the fields are about to ripen, and we are afraid that the birds will peck at the grains, so we built walls to defend them." The officer couldn't help but laugh and said, "Silly slaves, no matter how high you build the wall, the birds will fly down from above." The farmers continued to work as if they hadn't heard the officer's words.

The troops entered the city and encountered a person carrying a door panel, panting and walking towards them. The officer scolded, "What are you carrying the door panel for?" The man said, "I am going to a distant place. I have money hidden at home and I am afraid that thieves will steal it. I carried the door panel out, so the thieves cannot open the door and enter." The officer snorted and said, "You fool, if you leave the door at home and carry the money with you, wouldn't it be safer?" The man shook his head and just chuckled as he walked forward.

The officer led the troops along the street and saw that the people in the city were acting very foolishly. He said to the soldiers, "The people here are extremely foolish. If we punish fools, it would be embarrassing. We should report to the king and then decide on a solution." After speaking, he led the troops back to the palace and reported the situation he had seen to the king.

After hearing the officer's words, the king immediately pardoned the people of the entire city and did not cut off their noses.

After the publication of this book, Mr. Liu Yizheng criticized the above text, saying, "Should the king be learned? Should nose cutting be learned? Should the masses making it impossible for the king to enter the city be learned? Should pretending to be a fool to protect the nose be learned? Should scolding people as silly slaves be learned? Should the officer's reprimand be learned? Should the king's being deceived and pardoning the nose cutters be learned? I think not only the cruel things like nose cutting should not be told to children, but also the tone of scolding people should not be included in the science textbooks." (See Guofeng, Volume 5, Issue 1, and Jiangsu Education, National Language Education Special Issue, "Questions on National Language Teaching Materials.")

From this passage, it can be seen that Mr. Liu's insights are threefold: first, there are many things in "Wonderful Trick to Protect the Nose" that should not be learned; second, cruel things like nose cutting should not be told to children; and third, there should be no scolding tones in textbooks.

I will now reply to Mr. Liu:

(1) Learning is a kind of stimulus, and the reaction caused by the stimulus is nothing more than two kinds: one is to learn from good, and the other is to abandon evil. Learning from good is imitation, which is learning; abandoning evil is a warning, which is not learning. Teaching materials have both positive and negative aspects. Positive teaching materials stimulate children to do good, while negative teaching materials stimulate children to abandon evil. Although the paths are different, the purpose of education can be achieved in the same way. We know that the task of reading education in the national language subject is to cultivate reading ability and interest as the primary purpose. Moral training is, of course, not as strong as in civics and society, but the text "Wonderful Trick to Protect the Nose" also contains two levels of positive and negative effects. Mr. Liu poses several questions, meaning that he fears that children will learn bad things after reading it. In fact, from a negative perspective, children will definitely not learn from the king after reading it, even without discussion, because they know that the king's tyranny is a bad thing; they will definitely not learn to cut noses, because they know that cutting noses is a bad thing; they will definitely not learn to scold people as silly slaves; they will definitely not learn to reprimand, because they know that scolding and reprimanding are bad things. These four reactions of thinking that bad things should not be learned do not need any external evidence. Please ask yourself, Mr. Liu, whether you have this feeling after reading this lesson's text, or please ask children these questions to see if the children answer that they should not be learned. From a positive perspective, "the masses making it impossible for the king to enter the city" is because of resisting the king's harassment. Since the king cannot protect the people, the people will naturally rise up to resist. "Pretending to be a fool to protect the nose" is because of preventing the king's tyranny. Since the king is tyrannical, the people, in a position of powerlessness and courage, will naturally design to get rid of the tragedy of nose cutting. As a result, the king is deceived (it is a design to avoid disaster, not deception), and pardoning the nose cutters is the success of the people's design. We can use Dr. Sun Yat-sen's historical facts as proof for this example. Dr. Sun Yat-sen was engaged in revolution, resisting tyranny, for forty years as one day. In the middle, he did not hesitate to disguise and change his name in order to save his useful body and serve the country. It can be seen that reasonable resistance and situational adaptation are not things that cannot be learned. In short, positive teaching materials naturally account for the majority of a book, but adding some negative teaching materials with humor (this lesson's text, according to the curriculum standards, is literary in content and a joke or legend in form, and does not take moral training as the greatest goal) and containing the intention of abandoning evil, in order to change the children's daily taste for learning positive teaching materials, does not go against the principles of learning, and moreover, it also contains a positive effect.

(2) The forms of human society, "right" and "wrong," "good" and "evil," are relative. Since we have no way to make society all "right" and "good," how can children not know about "wrong" and "evil," making them become a first-class figure of "why not eat meat porridge" in the future, stepping into society to be a superman who knows "good" and "right" but does not know "evil" and does not know "wrong?" Cutting off noses is indeed an inhumane barbaric act, but records in Chinese and foreign history show that humans have indeed done such things. Even in today's civilization, our revolutionary martyr Cai Gongshi could not avoid having his nose cut off and his eyes gouged out by the brutal Japanese soldiers. Could it be that the tragic killing of Cai Gongshi by the Japanese soldiers will also be kept from children because of its cruelty? It should be known that the distinction between "good," "evil," "right," and "wrong" cannot be made clear without comparison. Knowing "good" to imitate, knowing "evil" to understand the warning, is really the same need in education.

(3) "Silly slave" and "reprimand" are both bad nouns, but there are indeed "silly slaves" in society, and there is indeed "reprimand" in human speech. If these words are not allowed for children to learn, then what will they think if they encounter others calling them "silly slaves" or "reprimanding" them? We have no practical way to make society have no "silly slaves" and no sounds of "reprimand." We also have no way to eliminate words such as "silly slave" and "reprimand" in the dictionary. Then, carefully not letting children know words such as "silly slave" and "reprimand" is not deceiving children?

In all fairness, the reason why high school national language teaching materials do not avoid jokes and legends is because these teaching materials, on the one hand, can meet the learning interests of children, and on the other hand, can cultivate children's reading ability. They do not violate and conform to the main purpose of national language teaching. Even if we take a step back and speculate on Mr. Liu's meaning, thinking that national language teaching materials must be conditioned on moral cultivation in every article, then, as mentioned above, "Wonderful Trick to Protect the Nose" does not go against the conditions of moral cultivation and has its own value to read. If we take only a part and use one or two nouns as criticism, we will lose the true attitude of scholars' comments. Mr. Liu has compiled and selected the Zhongshan National Language Reader for high schools. I randomly flipped through a few articles and found phrases such as "dismembered by five horses," "and even thought to restore corporal punishment," "although eating the flesh of the commentators does not help the people" (see Su Shi's Letter to Emperor Shenzong in the second volume), "cooking the talkers," "children are not enough to conspire with," "King Xiang glared at them" (see Historical Records of Xiang Yu in the second volume), and other words and sentences. If I criticize Mr. Liu by saying, "Not only the cruel things such as 'dismemberment by five horses,' 'corporal punishment,' 'eating human flesh,' and 'cooking' should not be told to students, but also the tone of scolding people and the strict words and colors should not be included in textbooks," wouldn't Mr. Liu burst out laughing?

The reply ends here. I hope that Mr. Liu and those who have a research interest in national language teaching can give their advice. (End)

A Fierce Football Battle: Tung Wah Powerfully Defeats Yu You 185

丨Result: Three to One丨

Tung Wah Wins with Balanced Performance

Yu You and Tung Wah, known as the two giants of Shanghai football, met at Shen Garden yesterday at 3 PM for a match in the Western League A Division. Considering the past performance of the two teams and their current talent, the attraction for the audience was undoubtedly amazing. Nearly 8,000 spectators were seated around the field, which was the expected turnout. Under tense circumstances, both sides frequently committed fouls, which was a flaw. Each side dominated for 45 minutes in each half. Tung Wah scored three goals in the first half, and Yu You scored one goal in the second half. The referee, Shen Huichun, handled the situation appropriately, so all parties were able to maintain peace.

Tung Wah Team:

Lu Zhongen, Li Ning, Chen Gong, Gu Shang, Feng Yunyou, Chen Hongguang, Cao Qiuting, Li Yichen, Dai Linjing, Chen Jiaqiu, Jia Youliang

Yu You Team:

Xu Heng, Wang Shusen, Jiang Shanjing, Liang Shutang, Chen Zhenxiang, Yun Feng, Fu Hexuan, Sun Jinshun, Luo Haiguang, Zhong Yuxiang, Zhong Yongshen

Too Much Pressure Among Family Members: Although the talents of the two teams are not all at their peak, they can be considered excellent. Some have attended the Far Eastern Games, and others have dominated Shanghai. Ordinary players are not on the field. They can be considered representative figures in today's Shanghai Chinese football scene, worthy of the title of heroes. However, the distinction between us and them is too strong, and the desire to win is even deeper. As a result, the artistic performance is diminished, and the focus shifts to defending against each other. Several times, fierce actions occurred, but they were still able to maintain the overall situation and end without incident. In the end, they are all family members, so why put so much pressure on each other?

Obvious Differences in Strength: Tung Wah benefited from balanced performance between the front and back lines, and the forwards cooperated more closely. Yu You's internal resistance was strong, but the forward attacks were slightly weaker. The two sides had the same opportunities, and the difference in victory and defeat was due to this. Speaking individually, the goalkeeper Xu Heng is still commendable. The inner guards were equally skilled. Chen Zhenxiang and Feng Yunyou in the center back line can be called comparable. The left and right supports were more solid for Tung Wah. Zhong Yongshen was the most effective among Yu You's five forwards. Sun Jin and Gu were under surveillance. Luo Haiguang was not used at the right time. Zhong Yuxiang could dribble but was not good at shooting. Fu Hexuan contributed very little. Tung Wah's two wings were more active. Li Yichen was competent, Chen Jiaqiu was steady, and Dai Linjing was clever. Therefore,

Tung Wah Scores in Seven Minutes: Not long after Yu You kicked off, they were attacked by Tung Wah. Jia Youliang passed to the central area. Xu Heng met and caught the ball. Fu Hexuan was ordered to counterattack. Gu Shang intercepted and passed to Dai Linjing. Jiang Shanjing chased after him quickly. The ball went from the end line to the central area. Yu You's goalkeeper and inner guards were paying attention to the left side and were caught off guard. Cao Qiuting had been waiting for a long time and kicked the ball into the goal, only seven minutes into the game, which was surprising.

Good Opportunities Misused: Once the victory and defeat were determined, the situation gradually worsened, and chaos occurred at any time. Fortunately, they managed to maintain the situation. Zhong Yongshen made two successful challenges at this time, causing some anxiety for Tung Wah, but they were able to turn the crisis into safety with tight defense. Jiang Shanjing also went to the enemy's position and shot, but the shot was too high, and Lu Zhongen caught it easily. Tung Wah suddenly changed tactics, switching from short passes to long passes. After three or four rotations, the ball was at Jia's feet. The goal was in sight, but he was too hasty and kicked it at an angle, allowing Yu You to invade again. Before long, the area within ten feet of Tung Wah's goal became a melee zone for both sides. Initially, it was caused by Zhong Yongshen's excellent corner kick, and the ball even hit the goalpost but did not go in. Yu You missed this good opportunity, causing the audience to regret it.

Yu You Loses Consecutive Goals Under Pressure: Tung Wah's crisis had just passed, and the morale of the army was boosted. Center forward Dai urged the troops to break into the enemy's position. Dust flew up, and Li Yichen was seen rushing in, but Jiang Shanjing could not stop him. He went to the front of the goal, and Xu Heng, who was always alert, could not stop him from entering. Tung Wah won the goal. After Tung Wah scored, Chen Hongguang committed a foul and was penalized. Sun Jinshun took a shot from 25 yards away from the goal. The ball was fast and low, but Lu had prepared early and caught it. The forwards surrounded the area but retreated without success. Dai and Li then advanced again. Cao Qiuting responded on the left. In an instant, Li Yichen shot suddenly, hitting Jiang's back squarely, and the ball bounced into the net. Xu Heng was unable to turn the tide. In the first half, Tung Wah scored three goals.

Regains One Goal in Revival: In the second half, Yu You's lineup was more organized and had a sense of revival. Sun Jinshun and Luo Haiguang shot one after another, but their ambitions were not realized. They were in a superior position but were repeatedly shut out because they did not shoot properly. Ten minutes into the second half, Chen Zhenxiang assisted in the central area, and Sun Jinshun used all his strength to score into the net, making it three to one. Later, Zhong Yongshen passed the ball into the center, but Luo and Fu lost their footing one after another. Zhong tried again, but Chen was slow and did not succeed. At that time, Chen Gong, Jiang Shanjing, Cao Qiuting and others were injured one after another, went out and came back in. Yu You had more opportunities to get the ball, but they could not reverse the situation because their forwards were not as good as the opponents. As a result, Tung Wah won three to one.

Jiangxi Women's Sports Meet Ends in Wind and Rain 186

One Central China Record Broken

Five Provincial Records Broken

(Nanchang Correspondence) The first Jiangxi Women's Sports Meet concluded on the 16th, which was the final day of the competition. On that day, the wind and rain were mixed, even worse than yesterday. Most people thought it would be postponed, but the athletes still arrived on time in the wind and rain. Although the weather was as cold as winter, everyone was in high spirits and fought fiercely. Compared to the seemingly weak young ladies, it was like heaven and earth. The whole day was for ball games. In volleyball, the girls' middle school team played against Baoling, and Baoling won overwhelmingly with a score of 21 to 12. In basketball, the women's vocational school team played against the midwifery school team. The midwifery school team was very weak and lost badly with a score of 4 to 49. When the ball games were over, Chen Mengyu, the principal of the Shanghai Dongya Sports Academy, assigned male students who graduated in Jiangxi to form groups with the female team members who came to Jiangxi for performances. The result was a tie with a score of 10 to 10. After the two teams finished performing, the Dongya team played another performance against the provincial basketball champion team (women's vocational school team). The women's vocational school team was obviously no match for them and lost miserably with a score of 3 to 29. However, this was expected. It was just "seeking advice."

The Shanghai Dongya team finished its performances in Jiangxi, and Qian Hangsu and 14 others returned to Shanghai on the 17th, led by Principal Chen. It is said that Anhui has also sent a letter inviting them to participate in performances, but it is unknown whether it will become a reality.

Second Day 187

The city was full of wind and rain near Chongyang. On this day, the north wind roared and drizzle fell. The audience in the public sports field was sparse, huddled up and shivering, while a group of athletes still wore short sleeves and shorts, fighting against the cold wind and rain. Around 9 o'clock, the sports events started, and the results were much better than last year. One Central China record was broken, and five provincial records were broken. The details are as follows:

Long Jump Breaks Central China Record: Tan Caiyun is a high-achieving student at the women's vocational school and has a considerable position in women's sports in the province. This time, she broke the previous Central China Games record in the long jump with a distance of 4.13 meters.

Five Provincial Records Broken: (1) In the Group B field events, Cheng Maolan threw the shot put 7.85 meters and the javelin 17.58 meters. (2) In the track events, Li Xiuqin broke the provincial record in the 50-meter dash with 8 seconds. Tan Caiyun set a new provincial record with 7.9 seconds. Tan Caiyun also broke the provincial record in the 100-meter dash with 15 seconds.

Shanghai Stars Give Wonderful Performances: Qian Hangsu is a short-distance running star, and the 100-meter dash is his specialty. He was the focus of everyone's attention. At the sound of the gun, Qian shot like an arrow and reached the finish line in 14 seconds. Wang Changhua, a member of the Dongya team, performed the high jump. He jumped one meter effortlessly. Finally, he jumped 1.29 meters. The 400-meter relay race was also performed by Qian Hangsu, Xu Yuan, Wang Changhua, and Chen Shuqing from the Dongya team. They struggled against the wind and rain and still maintained the national record.

Opening Highlights 188

The first Jiangxi Provincial Women's Sports Meet was opened at the provincial sports field at 9 a.m. yesterday (the 14th). However, the north wind was strong and dust filled the sky, which reduced the excitement. No less than 2,000 students from various girls' middle schools in Nanchang participated. Qian Hangsu and her group of 14 athletes from Shanghai also attended. There were thousands of guests and spectators from all walks of life. The audience on both sides of the rostrum was packed, making it an unprecedentedly lively event. The highlights of the day at the venue are recorded below:

The Venue Is Like Martial Law: In addition to the social boy scouts maintaining order at the venue, a team each of police, military police, security guards, and soldiers were responsible for guarding the venue. Therefore, there were layers of boy scouts, military police, police, and security guards guarding the entrances and exits of the venue, as if under special martial law. The spectators around were all surprised and whispered about it. Some joked that the organizing committee of the games was so careful in order to protect Miss Qian from Shanghai.

Everyone Is Looking for Miss Qian: The spectators at the venue all wanted to see Miss Qian. Therefore, the sound of "Which one is Miss Qian?" could be heard everywhere. Later, after the opening ceremony, reporters at the venue rushed to the rostrum to surround Miss Qian and take pictures. The audience's attention was focused on the rostrum, and they saw Miss Qian shyly answering in the midst of an onslaught of hand-held cameras.

Stars Display Their Calligraphy on the Spot: The day before the games, Jiangxi Minbao planned to publish a special edition for the Provincial Women's Sports Meet and asked Miss Qian to write a message in her own handwriting. Her calligraphy was delicate and beautiful. Therefore, guests and reporters from various newspapers at the venue also asked for her calligraphy. Miss Qian was generous and composedly wielded her brush at the venue, signing her name or writing inscriptions as requested.

The Chairman调酒水车 Distributes Water: On that day, the wind was strong and the venue was filled with sand, which made people feel disoriented. The chairman of the games, the Director of the Department of Education, Cheng Shizhuo, recognizing this, immediately asked the Municipal Committee to borrow a洒水马车 water truck after the opening ceremony to drive around the venue and moisten the soil. However, the north wind was too strong, so the effect was minimal.

Photographers Were Busy Taking Pictures: The Political Training Office of the 行营 Military Headquarters believed that the Nanchang Women's Sports Meet was an unprecedented and significant event. Therefore, they also came to the venue to film the event from beginning to end, keeping a group of photographers very busy. (October 15th)

On the Pathology of Protozoa (1) 197

— Zhu Yanggao

In the universe, in addition to the animals, plants, and minerals that we can see with the naked eye, there is another world, most of which cannot be observed without a microscope. The protozoa I want to talk about today belongs to this world. When you hear this term, you may think about what these animals look like. This is what I can guess. Originally, the organization of these animals is very simple. Not to mention that they have no head or tail, the structure of their whole body consists of only one cell. Therefore, they also belong to the category of so-called "unicellular organisms." "Organism" is a "living" thing, so how do they live? Can they eat? Breathe? Move? Reproduce? Of course, they can. Then, it is a bit doubtful. Can one cell have such great functions? Although we humans are the most evolved animals, we cannot find a cell in the human body that has so many physiological functions. This is not a good thing to say. Although a single cell is like this compared to a single cell, our human body organization has a large number, so there is a kind of collective structure (organ). A person is formed by integrating many organs to cooperate. Each organ's cell has its own specialized skills, just like a carpenter can only make tables and chairs, because he has not learned to be a blacksmith since he was young and cannot make knives. Besides, we already have a blacksmith in our body. But then again, we cannot help but wonder how one cell of the protozoa has so many physiological abilities.

Today, let's first look at the cell's organization, which is similar to that of other animals: (1) protoplasm, (2) cell nucleus. The texture of the protoplasm is a kind of gelatinous substance, between liquid and solid. Therefore, when this protozoa is still, it looks like a drop of glue and is perfectly round. As for its composition, it also contains proteins, fats, and lipids, etc. In addition, there are undigested foods and air bubbles, etc. that they take from the outside. This gelatinous substance is affected by air in the layer connected to the air, so it is relatively solidified and viscous, and it becomes a skin-like thing. The texture of this cell skin toward the inside gradually becomes thinner. When we observe its shape with a microscope, the protoplasm mostly looks like a honeycomb. A more important cell component than protoplasm is the cell nucleus. If we compare the cell nucleus to the nucleus in a fruit, then the flesh outside the fruit is like the protoplasm of the cell. The nucleus of the fruit is often more important than the outer flesh. The main ability to pass on genes is hidden in the nucleus. This goes without saying, everyone knows it. We must know that the nucleus of our protozoa is also exactly like this. Originally, the physiological work of reproduction and heredity of protozoa is entirely dependent on its nucleus to control everything. We only need to reveal the function of the nucleus of the simplest protozoa, and then we will know how one protozoa can become two. First, the cell nucleus must be divided into two parts, and then the protoplasm will also be divided into two. So the main leadership work is in the hands of the nucleus. The inside of the nucleus originally contains two kinds of substances, one is the genetic substance, and the other is the motor substance. This motor substance first regularly distributes its own mass inside the nucleus, with two ends like two poles, and the middle like a magnetic field. It is really like the pattern of iron filings controlled by the force of a magnet. The genetic substance gathers on the equator of this magnetic field. With the force in this field, it gradually divides the entire mass evenly into two parts, one part goes to the anode, and the other part goes to the cathode, gathering around the two poles. When this time comes, the responsibility of the motor substance is considered complete. Therefore, it also divides itself into two parts, and the genetic substances attached to the two ends separate, until the nucleus has completed this set of work, then the protoplasm is divided into two, becoming two protozoa. (To be continued)

The Attitude a Judge Should Have When Handling Medical Malpractice Cases 198

— Song Guobin

In recent years, medical malpractice disputes have emerged endlessly, and it is not uncommon for doctors and patients to meet in court. Medical professionals often, in addition to defending themselves in court, submit all the facts to formal medical organizations for a fair judgment. When medical organizations accept such cases, they base their decisions on the pleadings of both the plaintiff and the defendant, and also conduct on-site investigations. Then, they report the conclusions reached from a scholarly and factual perspective to the court for the judge's reference in making a judgment. The intention is good. However, according to reports from some accused doctors recently, a few judges disregard these documents that uphold justice. Their judgments are still based on subjective arbitrariness. At first, I was puzzled, then I thought about it, and then I realized that the judge's arbitrariness is not without reason. Please allow me to briefly state the reasons.

Medicine is the most profound science. When a doctor treats a patient, and unfortunately the patient dies, whether the cause is due to the incurable nature of the disease or the doctor's misdiagnosis, only those who are deeply knowledgeable in medicine can know. Judges in the court are undoubtedly well-versed in the law, but in medicine, they are laymen, no different from ordinary people. At this time, if a formal medical organization provides an expert report based on scholarly and factual assessments for reference, the help it provides to the judge's judgment is self-evident. As the saying goes: "Determine the crime based on the facts." This means that the law is merely a written document and depends on the user. One must conduct a detailed investigation beyond the law. Therefore, in medical malpractice cases, the expert reports from medical organizations have extremely significant reference value in making a judgment. If a judge suspects that this is a biased defense of colleagues and disregards it, relying only on simple legal clauses and the one-sided complaints of the patient's family, then the result of the judgment, even if one does not want it to deviate from the facts and medical science, how can it be avoided? This is one reason.

When people are in a state of great anger or extreme sorrow, their words are often biased and lose balance. Those who speak may be driven by momentary emotions, but those who listen must calm their minds and quiet their emotions to seek the true facts. Otherwise, few can avoid being moved and losing balance as a result. Law is what maintains justice. Therefore, the character for "law" (法) contains the element of "water" (水), which symbolizes fairness. It means that those who uphold the law must have a mind as calm as water before they can fully handle the task of hearing cases. Nowadays, the complaints of patients' families accusing doctors are undoubtedly filled with poignant and touching words. If the judge is unconsciously moved by their words, then they will first have sympathy for the patient's family, and naturally have dissatisfaction with the doctor. With sympathy and dissatisfaction arising in the mind, it is no wonder that the judgment cannot be fair. This is the second reason.

In today's Chinese society, the general public often harbors feelings of jealousy towards doctors. When a doctor has an accident, many people secretly rejoice, even if they do not say so. However, while this is not blameworthy in others, it is absolutely unacceptable in a judge. A judge must maintain a completely independent and impartial spirit in order to achieve the goal of great justice and impartiality. If their mindset fails to distinguish itself from the common customs, then their judgment will be no different from placing themselves in the position of the general public. This explains why a certain judge, when interrogating a certain doctor, said, "You doctors caused someone's death and still want to argue?" Using emotions and easily expressing sympathy for the patient's family or the general public is the same as being biased and detrimental to utmost fairness. This is the third reason.

Based on the above three points, one can understand that the judge's arbitrariness is not without reason. In order to maintain justice and protect the medical profession, we request the Judicial Yuan and the Ministry of Judicial Administration, the highest judicial organs, to instruct courts in various regions to seek the opinions of formal medical organizations as a basis before announcing judgments in cases involving medical malpractice disputes in the future. As for the judges themselves, they should maintain an attitude of impartiality and fairness and should not easily express sympathy for any party. In this way, the unjust cases in the medical field can be eliminated, and the law itself will further increase its sanctity. This is not only fortunate for the medical field, but also for justice.

Common Knowledge Q&A on Diseases (Continued) 199

— Cheng Hanzhang

(Question) Among the physical therapy methods, which is the most effective?

(Answer) Among the physical therapy methods, gastric lavage is the most effective. Wash the stomach every morning and before going to bed.

(Question) Which medications can be used for drug therapy?

(Answer) For drug therapy, to prevent putrefaction and fermentation of retained matter in the stomach, disinfectants such as sodium salicylate, salol, cresol, resorcin, menthol, and creosote can be used. They should all be prescribed by a doctor. To absorb water and gas, activated charcoal, bismuth subnitrate, kaolin, and magnesium peroxide are used.

(Question) Can hydrotherapy and electrical massage be used?

(Answer) To promote the tension and movement of the stomach muscles, these methods can be used.

(43) Stomach Cancer

(Question) What is cancer?

(Answer) Cancer is a malignant and toxic tumor that can cause cachexia and death.

(Question) What is stomach cancer?

(Answer) It is a disease in which cancer occurs in the stomach. It is most common in the elderly, around the age of forty or fifty. Stomach cancer is very common.

(Question) What are the causes of stomach cancer?

(Answer) The causes of stomach cancer are mostly related to hereditary factors. It can also develop from the scars of healed gastric ulcers. In families with stomach cancer, the disease is often passed down through generations.

(Question) What are the initial symptoms of stomach cancer?

(Answer) In the early stages, most people have no symptoms. There are only mild symptoms of indigestion, such as loss of appetite, a feeling of fullness in the stomach, heaviness in the stomach, belching, and constipation. However, when there is a sudden loss of weight, weakness (cachexia), and anemia, stomach cancer should be suspected.

(Question) Are there changes in digestion after stomach cancer develops?

(Answer) Generally, it is like ordinary indigestion, with a coated tongue, complaints of thirst, and decreased appetite, especially an aversion to meat. After eating, there is a feeling of pressure and fullness in the stomach, sometimes with persistent stomach pain. There is abnormal fermentation in the stomach, often with belching and frequent vomiting.

(Question) What other symptoms are there of stomach cancer?

(Answer) Bleeding in the stomach is another symptom of stomach cancer. However, the amount of bleeding is small, and occult blood must be found in the vomit and feces.

Page 16

(Question) Can stomach cancer spread to other organs?

(Answer) Stomach cancer can easily spread to other organs. The most common is metastasis to the liver. In addition, it can spread to the supraclavicular lymph nodes on the left side, peritoneum, omentum, abdominal lymph nodes, lungs, spine, bones, brain, ovaries, navel, etc.

(Question) Is there a specific location in the stomach where stomach cancer occurs?

(Answer) It is not fixed. Some occur in the cardia, some in the pylorus, and some in the gastric body.

(Question) How should stomach cancer be diagnosed?

(Answer) Diagnosis should be based on age, the severity of onset, weight loss, anemia, cachexia, vomiting, coffee-ground vomitus, lack of free hydrochloric acid, the presence of lactic acid bacteria, the location of the tumor, metastasis, etc. However, early diagnosis is difficult.

(Question) What diseases should stomach cancer be differentiated from?

(Answer) It should be differentiated from gastric ulcer, liver cancer, chronic gastritis, pancreatic cancer, transverse colon cancer, duodenal cancer, pyloric spasm, etc.

(Question) What is the degree of danger of this disease?

(Answer) Absolutely poor. Generally, once the characteristic symptoms appear, death occurs in an average of about one year.

(Question) What are the treatment methods for stomach cancer?

(Answer) One should always eat easily digestible porridge-like foods. Although meat is disliked, it must also be given, along with internal use of dilute hydrochloric acid and pepsin. Usually, carbohydrates are the main food. Most medications are ineffective. Early surgical operation is best. For stomach bleeding, apply an ice pack to the stomach and try hemostatic agents. Perform gastric lavage every morning and evening to prevent fermentation and stagnation. For stomach pain, use analgesics as a last resort.

Common Knowledge on Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Hygiene 200

— Tang Renzhen

(20) Explanation of Brain Leakage (Continued from Previous)

(2) Chronic Maxillary Sinusitis

Chronic maxillary sinusitis is mostly suppurative. Therefore, it is also known as chronic suppurative maxillary sinusitis or maxillary sinus empyema. The most common, largest, and easiest cause of its occurrence is when acute maxillary sinusitis is not treated properly, leading to a chronic condition. At this time, the natural opening of the maxillary sinus is closed, and the function of drainage is also hindered. The mucous membrane inside the sinus is generally swollen with inflammation, and sometimes becomes polypoid. In addition, chronic diseases of the teeth and alveolar ridge, unclean tooth extractions, maxillary bone fractures, traumatic injuries to the maxillary bone, foreign bodies in the maxillary sinus, tuberculosis, syphilis, malignant tumors, etc., can also cause chronic maxillary sinusitis.

The most obvious and painful symptoms of chronic maxillary sinusitis are headaches and neuralgia. Headaches are mostly localized in the forehead. Neuralgia is mostly supraorbital and infraorbital neuralgia. Patients often experience sleep disturbances, mental depression, memory loss, and other symptoms. The nasal cavity is often blocked. A mucopurulent or purely purulent discharge flows from the nose, with a putrid odor. At this time, the sense of smell is also reduced. When there is too much purulent discharge, the pus is often swallowed, irritating the mucous membrane of the stomach and causing chronic digestive diseases. When examining the nasal cavity with a nasal speculum, the mucous membrane of the middle and inferior turbinates can be seen to be generally red and swollen. The middle meatus is filled with pus. The pus is yellow or green and mostly flows forward from the nostril. If this disease lasts for a considerable period of time, mucous nasal polyps (commonly known as nasal fungi) can often occur near the middle meatus. Therefore, I once said in the section on "Nasal Polyps" that "nasal polyps are not a separate disease, but an inflammatory product of another disease." Now, it can probably be understood more clearly.

The course of chronic maxillary sinusitis is very slow, often lasting for more than ten years. The best treatment method is to have a detailed examination by a specialist physician and carefully perform puncture and lavage or radical surgery. (To be continued)

Common Treatment Methods for Fever (4) 201

— Li Xing

In the case of short-term fever, even if the body does not receive sufficient nutrients, the body can sacrifice its own cells as fuel to barely get through. After recovery, the existing losses can be replenished. In the case of long-term fever, such as pulmonary tuberculosis, typhoid fever, heart inflammation, and prolonged pneumonia, if the food supplied during the illness does not contain enough nutrients, the body will initially become thin and then, due to a lack of nutrients, the ability to resist bacteria will be reduced. It is like an army lacking all supplies during a war; military failure is inevitable. If the body lacks resistance when sick, a minor illness will naturally become a serious illness, and a serious illness will be overwhelming. More than twenty years ago, doctors often starved feverish patients to reduce their fever. However, in recent years, it has been known that this theory is completely wrong. Today, through experience and research, it has been confirmed that if feverish patients are provided with a scientific diet that supplies all the nutrients needed by the body, the outcome of the disease will be much better, and many deaths can be avoided. Even for the same disease that used to be fatal, the new treatment method can bring life from death. Some people ask how it can be proven that the new medical method is correct and the old medical method is wrong? According to American medical statistics, twenty years ago, the mortality rate of typhoid fever was 20% (i.e., on average, twenty out of every hundred people with typhoid fever died). Recent statistics show that the mortality rate of typhoid fever is 10%. Although there have been various advances in recent treatment methods, the biggest advance in the case of typhoid fever lies in the scientificization of the patient's diet.

Some people ask what is meant by the scientificization of diet? Now we know that a car uses a certain amount of gasoline, oil, and water to travel a certain distance. For example, a large car consumes one gallon of gasoline every ten miles, a medium-sized car consumes one gallon of gasoline every twenty miles, and a small car consumes one gallon of gasoline every forty miles. In recent years, medical research has revealed the metabolism, heat generation, and energy generation of the human body, as well as the role of diet in the body, and the specific amount of diet needed at a specific time. Knowing a person's height, weight, age, and gender, one can know how much food must be used to make the body's nutrients suitable. Organic chemistry has shown us what chemical components are in what foods, how much heat is generated by how much food, and how much energy is generated. Our understanding of the human body's food needs is almost the same as calculating for a car or a machine. Ordinary people naturally think it is very miraculous, but it is only the culmination of countless scientific and medical research in recent decades.

The heat value of food is called calories. This is like measuring rice with a dou and a sheng. One calorie (large calorie) is the amount of heat that can raise the temperature of one thousand cubic centimeters (cc) of water by one degree (Celsius). The calorie value of food is calculated by burning the food with a standard electrical device and measuring the total amount of heat generated, in calories. This is the method used to calculate the heat value of food in the body. One gram of carbohydrate (starch and sugar) or one gram of protein can generate four calories of heat. One gram of oil or fat can generate nine calories of heat. For example, one pound of bread can generate 1260 calories of heat. One egg can generate 70 calories of heat. A small bowl of cooked rice can generate more than 200 calories of heat. A cup of milk can generate 160 calories of heat.

Now that the calorie value of food is known, the second step is to know how much food a person needs to meet their consumption, and to what extent they need to be fed when they have a fever so that they do not damage their own cells. How can they have sufficient supplies to overcome the bacteria and recover from the disease? Through years of research by physiologists, we already know the specific needs of the human body. For example, a person weighing 150 pounds needs 1770 calories for 24 hours of rest. A seamstress needs 2240 calories. A shoemaker needs 2600 calories. A machinist needs 3000 calories. A carpenter needs 3300 calories. A stonemason needs 4300 calories. A sawyer needs 4900 calories. This is why a dockworker eats more food in one day than a sedentary person eats in three days. As mentioned in the previous article, when a person has a fever, their body needs more nutrients. Each degree of fever increases the need by 10%. A patient with typhoid fever needs approximately 3000 calories of nutrients in 24 hours. If they do not eat any food for a day, they must turn their body cells into fuel for the body. One day is not a big deal. In ten or twenty days, if there are not enough nutrients, the body will naturally become thin to the extreme. From this, it can be seen that insufficient diet will definitely reduce the patient's resistance. If the body is supplied with all the necessary nutrients using medical methods, the body's resistance will be sufficient, and there will be more certainty of overcoming the disease.

Whether the diet is appropriate for a fever of one or two days is not important, but it is extremely important for long-term fever, because whether the nutrients are sufficient or not is extremely related to the turning point of the disease. Another thing to note is that feverish patients have poor appetites, and it is necessary to give them a proper diet to be beneficial. The proper diet is described below.

Fluids: Adequate fluids are the most needed thing for feverish patients. We know that water is the best solvent. During a fever, the body's blood is full of toxins and waste. Toxins come from bacteria, and waste is the result of chemical metabolism in the body. The higher the fever, the more chemical activity in the body, and the more waste. If these toxins and waste are fully dissolved by water, they can be excreted through urination, defecation, skin, sweating, or lung respiration. The better the excretion function, the easier it is for the disease to heal. Conversely, if the body lacks water and cannot excrete toxins and waste, the disease will naturally worsen. In addition to this reason, water is an indispensable element of life, and it is indispensable for all parts of the body. If it is lacking, it will stop functioning. When fever causes sweating or diarrhea, the water in the body is used up; if the stomach lacks water, it cannot produce gastric juice, and digestion stops. If the salivary glands lack water, not only cannot food be digested, but it is also not easy to swallow. For example, during cholera, because the water in the body is vomited and excreted from the body, the lack of water in the blood causes the blood to be particularly thick, and the blood flow stops, resulting in loss of life. Since water is so important, it must be supplied to the patient sufficiently. Give him water every one or two hours, not only without waiting for him to drink, but not even allowing his tongue, head, or lips to feel dry. The hotter the patient is, the more delirious he is and the less he knows he wants to drink water. If he cannot drink water himself, special methods must be used to supply his body with water. The best drink for patients is cold boiled water.

If you want to know if the patient's drinks are enough, you can measure how much urine he passes in a day and night. One thousand cc (about two pounds) is enough. Less than one thousand cc is not enough. The less the urine, the more the body lacks water. The remedy is to give him more water. Sometimes patients cannot drink water and the following methods must be used to add water to the body: (1) Irrigate the large intestine with water to make it absorbed into the body. Glucose can also be added to the water. Two or three times a day. (2) Inject saline solution under the skin. (3) Inject saline solution or glucose water or glucose saline solution intravenously. If these methods are used properly, they can sometimes have the effect of bringing back the dead.

Proper Food: Food is as urgent as drinks. Patients with fever have poor appetites, and ordinary food cannot be eaten. Patients are using all their strength to fight bacteria, so their digestive function is also very weak. Therefore, it is necessary to provide fully proper food, otherwise the patient cannot get sufficient nutrients. Patients should be provided with digestible food that is rich in starch and sugars, because these are important raw materials needed for fever. Note that if you give the patient indigestible food, it is better not to give him food at all. In short, the food needed by patients is (1) easy to digest (2) liquid food (3) raw materials for generating energy and heat (4) the patient has weak digestive power, so give him less food each time (5) the patient needs a large amount of nutrients, so give less food each time, and give several meals a day. Give him some food every one or two hours, eight to ten meals a day for people with high fever. Note that do not wake the patient up to eat when he is sleeping, because sleep is also essential for the body.

The following foods can be given to him two or three items at a time according to the patient's appetite: a bowl of thin porridge with a spoonful of sugar. Orange juice or oranges. Any fruit, one cup at a time, one cup of milk at a time. If you cannot afford milk, a small bowl of soy milk is similar in function to milk. Eggs can be poured with boiling water, soft-boiled, steamed, or eaten raw. Lotus root powder soup with sugar. Cooked fruits, such as pears and peaches, watermelon juice. Lemonade with sugar, grape juice, pineapple juice, rice soup, noodle soup with sugar. Various vegetable soups. Ice cream, chicken soup, fish soup, and meat soup are very good but should not be overdone. Tea or coffee with milk and sugar. The patient should be given high-quality food. Note that spoiled food will make a sick person sick and a sick person die. Tea or coffee should not be given to the patient at night because tea and coffee are stimulating and can easily cause the patient to lose sleep. Those who are used to drinking alcohol do not need to quit when they are sick. Although alcohol has a few harmful effects, it can also generate heat in the body. As the disease gradually recovers, the diet can gradually increase from liquid to soft foods, and finally gradually return to the usual diet. (To be continued)

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (26) 202

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter 8 Clinical Examination Methods

(1) Past History: The methods used by doctors to diagnose diseases are certainly complex and unusual, but in fact, they can be divided into two things: first, questioning, and second, examination. The past history presented in this section is entirely obtained through questioning procedures. What is past history? The scope included in this aspect is also very broad. The doctor should ask about the patient's name, age, address, occupation, gender, usual living conditions, habits, whether there are hereditary diseases, and the symptoms from the past to the present, without being annoyed by trivial details. Pulmonary tuberculosis is a very complex chronic disease (sometimes it can become a lifelong disease), and the various causes and consequences of it cannot be ignored. The few things to ask about, on the surface, seem to have little to do with the disease itself, but they are actually the first step in the doctor's diagnosis of a disease. Just take pulmonary tuberculosis as an example. There are already many examples in this area. We know that this disease can invade at any age, but the nature of the disease is not without distinction. For example, the disease in middle-aged people is mostly chronic, and the prognosis is better. In infants under two years old, it is acute, and the prognosis is extremely poor. In adolescents from three or four years old to fifteen or sixteen years old, the invasion of this disease is better, but in the ten years after that, it is completely different! These are all differences that occur due to different ages. Stoneworkers and tobacco workers who inhale harmful dust are more susceptible to invasion than others. This is a difference that occurs due to occupation. Big cities are worse than rural areas, and industrial areas are even worse; low, humid, and dirty houses are worse than houses with sunlight and air circulation. This is a difference that occurs due to address. The aspect of living conditions and habits is also obvious. People who are mentally and physically overworked are certainly more susceptible to invasion, and those who have a habit of smoking and drinking are worse than those who do not. These real examples can be seen by everyone. As for the examples of past diseases, that is even more obvious. Diseases such as rickets, pertussis, pneumonia, pleurisy, measles, syphilis, and influenza are all very easy to induce this disease. In particular, exudative pleurisy is almost 95% causally related to this disease. Based on these examples, we can at least know that the doctor's inquiry about past history is a very meaningful work and is indispensable for the initial stage of diagnosing a disease.

In addition to the various things mentioned above, there are several other things that should not be easily overlooked when inquiring about the past history of pulmonary tuberculosis. These should also be specifically mentioned here. These include the women's menstrual status, puerperal condition, whether the baby is healthy, whether the nutrition is natural or artificial; diseases other than this disease in the past, the signs of past tuberculosis and glandular diseases, the specific causes of the current disease, the patient's economic situation, the opportunity for infection, trauma, the signs of the initial disease, the symptoms, and the detailed course of treatment. Each and every real situation in these is related to the current disease itself. Both the doctor and the patient should pay attention to it without being annoyed by the complexity of the matter.

Five Years of the Sino-French University Pharmacy Department (2) 203

— Jin Ru

(3) Facilities (1) School Buildings: The school buildings are located at 410 Avenue Albert, French Concession, Shanghai. This is the former site of the Tongji Medical and Engineering School, situated between Rue Gan Shi Dong and Avenue Albert. To the right is the Mingfu Library, and to the left is the Sino-French National Engineering College. The area covers eight acres, four fen, and five li. There is a square athletic field covering one acre. There is a one-story building and two German-style buildings, built in 1908. According to the Treaty of Versailles after World War I, these were allocated for joint Sino-French cultural and educational endeavors. Originally, it was part of the Sino-French National Engineering College's facilities, managed by the college. They were lent to the Joint Sericulture Improvement Association as a clubhouse. When the specialized course was first established, it rented the left side of the Sericulture Improvement Association's building, consisting of only three classrooms and one each for the laboratory, office, and storage of medicines and equipment. By the autumn of 1919, due to an increase in practical courses, the buildings were insufficient. The school authorities then negotiated with the Sericulture Improvement Association to rent a portion of the two-story building on the right and the entire ground floor, totaling fourteen rooms. The various laboratories were reorganized. In 1920, the school again obtained the consent of the Sericulture Improvement Association, and the Sino-French National Engineering College issued a letter agreeing to allocate the entire western portion of the building to the department as permanent school buildings. This is the current school building, which was reported to the ministry for record in 1921. It includes seven large laboratories, four classrooms, a library, a balance room, an equipment storage room, a medicine storage room, a school supplies storage room, a faculty lounge, a student lounge, an exercise room, a general office, a garage, a kitchen, a dining hall, and a reception room, each with one room, and two faculty preparation rooms.

(2) Dormitories: Starting in the autumn of 1920, male and female dormitories were added. The male dormitory is located at 6-7 Rue de Sieyes, West Sieyes Lane, two three-story Western-style buildings. There are fourteen bedrooms of varying sizes. The larger rooms can accommodate six people, and the smaller rooms can accommodate four people. There are four bathrooms, two washrooms, a reception room, and a dormitory supervisor's room, each with one room. The female dormitory is located south of the school at 20 Bu Gao Lane, Avenue Albert, two two-story buildings. The internal layout is similar to the male dormitory, but on a smaller scale. In the summer vacation of 1920, the dormitory was expanded by renting 6-8, Lane 17, Rue de Sieyes, three three-story Western-style buildings, which can accommodate approximately fifty students.

(3) Medicinal Garden: In 1921, a medicinal garden was added to cultivate Chinese and foreign medicinal plants for research by faculty and students. It is located behind Jinan University in Zhenru, covering approximately twenty acres. A specialized worker was hired to cultivate the land and be responsible for guarding it. Currently, the planted medicinal herbs include Datura, foxglove, lavender, black horehound, white horehound, apple eggplant, wild cherry, mustard, safflower, and more than ten other types.

(4) Laboratories: When the department was first established, the regular course admitted one class of first-year students. The practical courses were divided into qualitative analytical chemistry, inorganic chemistry, and plant specimen preparation. Due to the cramped school buildings, the laboratory was simple, with only one large room downstairs, which is now the qualitative analytical chemistry laboratory. In July 1919, two major sections were added: one for animal, microscope, and physiology practical rooms, and the other for crude drug and pharmaceutical practical rooms. Other facilities such as the physics laboratory (darkroom, spectrometer, etc.), chemistry laboratory, preparation room, and storage room were gradually established and improved annually according to the volume of the school building and the needs of the curriculum. Currently, they are divided into three departments: physical chemistry, animal and plant, and pharmaceutical preparation. There are seven laboratories in total: a physics laboratory, an inorganic and organic chemistry laboratory, a qualitative and quantitative analytical chemistry laboratory, an animal and plant laboratory, a microbiology laboratory, a pharmaceutical chemistry laboratory, and a dispensing laboratory. All equipment, light intensity, and the height and orientation of the tables and cabinets have been meticulously designed to meet the needs of various experiments. Separate instrument, medicine, and specimen storage rooms are provided, with each section's teaching assistant responsible for management. It is said that the department plans to add three to four more laboratories, but has not yet started due to economic difficulties.

(5) Instruments and Specimens: Instruments such as colorimeters, spectrometers, polarimeters, and other experimental supplies are mostly purchased from France. Specimens are mostly collected from Germany. Chemical reagents that are needed temporarily are purchased locally. When the department was established, over 30,000 yuan was spent on purchasing instruments and specimens from Germany and France. Donations from domestic and foreign pharmaceutical factories and merchants also amounted to about 10,000 yuan. In 1922, another 10,000 yuan was spent on purchasing instruments from France. This amount was subsidized by the Shanghai French Municipal Council. This summer vacation, the Ministry of Education approved a subsidy of 10,000 yuan in national currency annually for library and instrument equipment. The department plans to use 30% of this specifically for purchasing instruments or specimens. Combined with the Municipal Council's subsidy of 10,000 yuan, the annual equipment budget for instruments and specimens will be 13,000 yuan in the future.

Literary Supplement

Small Western Paradise 204

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 3: Not Yet Understanding the Wandering, Peeking; Young Girl Wishes to Hear of Hardships, Visiting the Poor

It is just such a black 馍, half a bowl of cold water, squatting on the ground to eat. If it is in a circle surrounded by four or five people, there are also two earthenware dishes, one large and one small. In the large dish is a small handful of chives, which a person with a large mouth can simply swallow in one gulp. In the small dish is some chili powder, mixed with liquid. According to the rules of poor people in the Northwest for eating chili, that is probably vinegar. Watching them eat, they use the tips of their chopsticks to pick up a piece of chive, put it in their mouths and slowly chew it, and then pick up some chili powder and spread it on the cold 馍, and eat it like that. Some people use the palm of their hand to hold some salt, and mix it with the chili powder in the water and stir it. Immediately, the white water turns into a color that is neither red nor black; presumably that is considered a bowl of soup. Cheng Zhiqian was watching, somewhat lost in thought, when he saw a young carpenter walk in from outside, holding a small paper package in his hand, raising it high, and greeting his companions. Immediately, two or three people stretched out their necks and shouted, "Give me a little, give me a little." Seeing that person sit down among his companions, cautiously opening the paper package. Cheng Zhiqian strolled behind them to see what it was, and it turned out to be a small teaspoon of white sugar. In Jiangnan, it would be worth at most one small copper coin. But this craftsman held this slightly grayish sugar in his hand, and divided it in half with his chopsticks, making two portions. The larger portion was poured into the bowl of water in front of him. The smaller portion was handed to an older companion next to him. He himself used his chopsticks to stir the large half bowl of sugar water greatly for a while, and then held it in one hand and picked up the black 馍 in the other. He took a bite of the 馍, and used his lips to sip a little sugar water and swallowed it. Seeing how much he valued that half bowl of sugar water, it was no less than a bowl of ginseng soup. Just at this time, a large fat man, with a protruding belly, walked over. Seeing him wearing a set of student uniform made of sesame tweed, in this city of Xi'an, he was already considered a modern figure. (4-5)

Grinding Ink 205

— Written by Huo Xueming

Most writers nowadays use Western paper and blue ink when writing manuscripts; naturally, there is no need to grind a stick of pine soot ink in the inkstone. Moreover, writing with a fountain pen is indeed much simpler and faster than writing one word and dipping the brush in ink each time. I have never seen the words on the manuscripts of my friends more regular and beautiful than the original manuscript of "Haishang Flower" by Mr. Zeng Mengpu, the "Sick Man of East Asia" (seen at Mr. Zhang Ruogu's place). Mr. Zeng's solemnity and calmness when writing his novel can be seen in his meticulously written regular script, as delicate as an examination paper.

Thus, I imagined Mr. Zeng in his exquisite study, sitting by the bright window, how he raised his brush to write his article. The fragrance of flowers outside the study, gently flowing, good birds singing quietly, the fragrance of ink lightly drifting, at this time, he was seriously but also briskly creating an immortal masterpiece. Alas, I regret not taking a trip to Changshu for his sixtieth birthday two years ago.

And myself? Every morning, I also enjoy copying a little from stone rubbings. If a young person can cultivate his mind, practicing writing Chinese characters is the most effective method. Therefore, every evening, after writing, when reading ancient books, I use my idle right hand to effortlessly grind ink on the inkstone, circling it around and around.

Grinding ink also requires art. At least warriors or impatient people cannot grind ink. To grind good ink, one must be calm, focused, and serene, to grind it finely, evenly, richly, and clearly. There is no environment more comfortable than reading under the lamp and smelling the fragrance of ink. As for saving time and adding to the pleasure, those are secondary matters.

I remember that Mr. Qin Wenyi of my hometown used to have two lines of ink inscription saying: "It is not the person grinding the ink, but the ink grinding the person." That truly expresses the sentiments of a scholar. I don't know how many years I will have to be ground into a skeleton by ink.

Drops 206

— Shu Fan

Mid-Autumn Festival: The well-behaved dragon breathes and kisses the cool autumn, leisurely the bright pearl floats on the sea, three sheng of white dew flow through the lungs, do not let it condense into sorrow.

Insomnia: Lying awake without a candle, connecting to the market garden, myriad insects do not hinder the bean fence, three years of wind and dew sorrow this night, six months of rivers and lakes end my cold officialdom, bowing my head in shame to see the tall willow shadows, my wanderings too lazy to examine my hermit's cap, the new method of poverty and hunger I can explain, the large moon and many stars, I will fight them myself.

A Pilgrimage to the Twenty-Two Story Building 207

— Zixin

How fortunate it is, the greatest, most sublime building, in Shanghai, the leader of all buildings, the twenty-two story building – to be able to visit it on a cloudy afternoon.

The bottom floor is very messy, under renovation. The folding doors of the three elevators, painted a light green base, covered with golden flowers, very rich and magnificent. The elevators rise and fall more smoothly and quickly than usual, without changes in the brightness of the lights, perhaps one might even think they are still stationary when rising!

The elevator route only reaches the eighteenth floor, and no further – in the corner of the twentieth floor is the main control system for the elevators. When the elevators rise and fall, the huge wheels turn very quickly. This is so much like the process of life – advancing forward. The rooms of the International Hotel, teak floors, teak doors, inlaid with sparkling mirrors, bathrooms, toilets, all exceptionally clean, everywhere revealing the extravagance of the city, making people envious.

Standing on the top floor, looking into the distance, everything is a hazy white, the sky and earth mixed together; the houses all look like chicken coops, the vast racecourse, green grass revealing the white and gray lines of the tracks, exactly like a natural oil painting; the roads seem to have shrunk a lot, the vehicles moving, also losing their original state of being small and elongated. The wind is especially strong and forceful, there are railings around, looking down at the bottom floor, one's legs tremble uncontrollably, shrinking back, even though one is a enjoyer, with no danger involved, still so timid, trembling, shrinking back, recalling the creators at that time, what their situation was really like, one wonders. The golden ball at the very top, surrounded by small pieces of magnetic stone, brushed with a golden powder, shows its arrogance in the clouds.

Once it's completed, perhaps we won't be allowed to leave our footprints freely anymore!

New Poems of the Emerald Pavilion 208

— Ms. Chen Xiaocui

(The posthumous portrait of Ms. Xindan was painted by Zhang Daqian for Lu Danlin)

Having washed away the makeup, she is pitiable in her simplicity. The round fan in her sleeve has been there for three years. May her graceful image remain in the next life. In the ancestral temple among the willows, worship the water fairy.

Why was the jade concubine banished to the riverbank? Returning her bright pearl, only tears remain. It's better to let the painter have the good fortune. In the morning, he personally paints her long eyebrows.

The musk, ground into dust, gives off a fragrance even in death. News from the sea and mountains is cut off, no longer heard. I'll use ten thousand entangled words. To inscribe on the beautiful woman's white silk skirt.

Early on, she knew that life and death return to the great transformation. The hardest thing is to find a confidante among the beautiful. An ordinary sheet of xuan paper. Can convey emotions with the arch of her eyebrows.

Floating clouds and bright moon meet in the sky. The small fan and simple dress are a dream. Every time I write, I think of the horizon. No need to abruptly call her Zhenzhen.

Records of Royal Fragrances 209

— Original work by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Because the Beijing-Fengtian Railway was built along the coastline, we could often see the coast of Liaodong Bay flickering in our eyes as we looked east from the train.

My feelings after entering the three northeastern provinces were very complex: but the deepest point was that I felt that the situation here still could not get rid of a kind of original wildness. I think that is correct! Because hundreds or thousands of years ago, our ancestors were originally a very strong and untamed people; relying on their strong physique and courageous胆力, they roamed freely in this vast wilderness. Except for a part of what they used daily which was grown from the fields, the rest was obtained from hunting; in this way, the combat power of this nation was strengthened unintentionally, and later they were able to conquer the entire territory of China proper with tens of thousands of troops, without much effort. Although the Bannermen in the interior have gradually become weak, the people in the three northeastern provinces outside the customs still retain some of the heredity of the nomadic people – brave and rough.

Along the way, we also passed several county towns scattered on both sides. These county towns were very small and far from the tracks. Looking at them from the train, they seemed to be at the end of the horizon. If it weren't for Zhang De, the more familiar eunuch, pointing them out to us, we would never have thought that a black mass of shadows was a county town, and 99% of the time we would have thought it was a large rock that had collapsed from the mountain.
