Biographical Notes

Wang Ziping's Adventure in Jinan 211

— Zhang Zhenlü

When the news that Zhang Xuebin was setting up a boxing ring in the Greater Shanghai Garden spread throughout Shanghai, I couldn't help but think of martial artist Wang Ziping's amazing adventure in Jinan. I'm afraid very few people know about this, although it happened ten years ago, I will record this old news here, which can also be considered as keeping up with the times.

One day, I went to visit my friend Jin Wentao; he had also put in a lot of effort in martial arts and had unique achievements. Now he lives in seclusion in Shanghai, only using his very effective massage skills to treat people and support himself. That day, I saw a guest with a short and sturdy figure, dark complexion, bright eyes, speaking with a northern accent, silent and taciturn. The posture he was sitting in was as stable as iron, his bearing serious, different from ordinary people. After a while, he left. I eagerly asked Brother Wentao: "Is that person Wang Ziping?" Because I knew that he and Wang were like-minded comrades, he smiled and nodded. Discussions about all things martial arts then took place, and in narrating Wang Ziping's life, I especially felt that the "Jinan incident" was worth noting and remembering.

That year, Wang Ziping was hired by the highest military authority of Shandong Province to train a group of lower-ranking officers in martial arts, with the honorable title of coach. There was more than one coach, and the rest all admired Wang, and in daily life, they all expressed special respect to him. Among them, there was a certain foreign coach, who did not see any special talents in Wang, and was very suspicious of the attitude of his peers. He alone refused to accept it and showed contempt. Someone told him: "This Coach Wang is famous throughout the country and has real skills." He immediately found Wang and wanted to compete with him. Wang was originally the most peaceful and humble person, believing that he was merely living up to a false reputation, and declined the match. That foreigner thought he was just pretending to be modest and despised him even more. In his daily speech, he often used insulting tones and threatened to compete at every turn. Finally, one day, both parties invited witnesses and signed a contract stating that if there was any accidental injury, it was all considered fate. Under duress, Wang sent that foreign coach to his death with one punch.

Among the witnesses was also a staff member of a certain foreign consulate. At first, because he knew that the coach's skills were already at home, there was no danger to his life, but when he sacrificed under a fair punch, he could only feel frustrated and had nothing to say. However, a group of foreign students, who had been taught martial arts by that coach, secretly plotted revenge day and night, also harboring the side effect of eliminating outstanding talents from our country. Someone secretly told Wang to take precautions, but he believed that humans always value reason, and that no civilized country would do barbaric things, so he did not worry at all; in fact, because he had skills, he was confident that he could defend himself, so he was inevitably arrogant.

One day, Wang went to a movie theater as usual for entertainment. Not long after the movie started, he happened to look back and saw, by the light of the movie, that the ten rows behind his seat were full of uniformed foreign students. He immediately became alert and weighed how he could resist if there was any trouble, being alone and unarmed. While he was hesitating, a flashlight suddenly shone on him, and a gunshot rang out. Fortunately, he was short in stature, and immediately squatted down, avoiding the first bullet; then, like an arrow flying off the string, his body shot straight to the empty stage in front, actually leaping over the heads of people in nearly ten rows of seats. Without hesitation, amidst a hail of gunfire, he leaped from the stage to the central gallery, his toes touching the backs of the seats, and in three or two leaps, he reached the side of the wall. He didn't hesitate even more, and with three or two punches, he knocked a big hole in the brick wall, retreated slightly, put his body diagonally through it, jumped out of the window into the street, and fled away! There were also one or two foreign students standing guard in front of the theater door, only preventing the opponent from escaping from the main entrance, preparing to intercept them head-on. How could they have expected a Flying General to descend from the sky? In the confusion and panic, they drew their guns and chased after him, but it was already too late.

Having experienced this dangerous situation, Wang deeply regretted the immorality of the certain foreign national character, and only then did he feel that this Jinan was not his comfortable hometown. He also did not want the government to handle this weak country diplomacy for him, so he hurriedly resigned from his position as coach and quietly left.

Economic Journal

China's Monetary Panic 212

— Lecture by G.E. Hubbard, Translated by Xie Juceng

Since the announcement of the silver export tax rate on October 15th, the market has undergone significant changes in the past three or four days. The primary reason for this, in my opinion, is due to speculative merchants alarming each other, creating something out of nothing. Mr. G.E. Hubbard, a well-known foreign exchange broker in Shanghai, gave a detailed explanation based on his extensive experience and calm mind at the Rotary Club on the 18th. His words were of great value, and are hereby introduced to the readers of this publication.

Sincerely, Juceng

The currency panic in China began to show signs a few years ago, entirely due to the impact of the world economic panic, and not due to China's own faults. When the world economic panic erupted at the end of 1929, our observation was that the first commodity to quickly decline in price was silver. There is a saying in society – I don't know what principle it's based on – that the wholesale prices of all commodities in the world can be represented by silver. When you see the price of silver falling, you can see the prices of other goods also falling. When the price of silver rises, the prices of other goods also rise. As for which of these many commodities is affected first, it's hard to say. However, according to the charts I have compiled, it can be proved that the above observation is correct. And in any case, we saw the price of silver fall to such an extent in 1929, 1930, and 1931 that everyone couldn't help but be surprised. Whether this situation is good or bad depends on the situation, and I dare not guess arbitrarily. What I say is fair and unbiased. At that time, many worried friends strongly advocated implementing a silver import tax, or even prohibiting the import of silver, so that the world could no longer dump silver into China. I immediately felt that this was not a smart solution, because there is no such thing as dumping for silver. Goods may be dumped, but as for silver, the more China has, the better. At that time, Finance Minister Song Ziwen took no action on this, which deserves our praise. As a result, China benefited greatly from allowing the free inflow of silver into the country, receiving a lot of silver.

In the past twelve years – from 1921 to 1933 – Shanghai, the financial center of China, imported silver from overseas and inland areas worth approximately 550,000,000 yuan. However, we transported more to the inland areas than was transported out of them. The effect of the financial authorities allowing the free import of silver was that, except for a very small number of people close to the New York Stock Exchange, no one believed that there was a world economic panic. Wholesale prices in China did not fall but rose, so China became the only country in the world to avoid being shrouded in recession. This trend remained consistent until 1932. From that time on, beginning with Britain's departure from the gold standard in 1931, followed by Japan, China began to suffer a major blow. Later, in 1933, the United States followed suit, and we felt the impact becoming more and more serious, because the purchasing power of the US and Britain was reduced compared to before. In other words, since 1933, prices in China have gradually fallen, putting China in a position difficult to curb deflation. The so-called deflation means that China cannot even maintain its small export trade, and imports are booming, so that the situation is getting more and more serious. I cannot say that we immediately feel a significant impact due to the trade deficit; but people saw that the situation was getting worse and worse, and clearly saw that some things were being reversed, so they became suspicious.

We have seen capital flowing out of China. Originally, in the previous few years – 1930, 1931, 1932 – many foreign companies here kept their private funds in China, and even remitted funds from abroad to China. Because they said, "We want to wait for a better exchange rate, and China is in a good economic position." But as soon as they saw that the situation was not right, they couldn't help but start to worry, so they moved all of their silver supply back to their home countries, or left Chinese ports. Just starting from April this year – there was no movement in January to March – silver began to be exported. Based on the published statistics I have collected and calculated, I am confident that China owns at least 2 billion ounces of silver – including the three northeastern provinces and Mongolia. China has lost silver worth 200 million yuan in the recent past six months. This number cannot be said to be small, but if we consider that China has received silver from foreign countries worth as much as 550 million yuan in the past twelve years, this situation does not seem very significant. The only problem is that by this time, there is already a lack of public confidence.

You often hear that China needs to ship silver to balance the trade deficit, and I also admit that there is this need. But I dare say that the silver shipped for export is actually used to offset the trade deficit, but accounts for only a very small portion, of which 75 percent belongs to the outflow of capital. Generally speaking, once a panic begins, this kind of thing is difficult to curb.

Whether the Chinese government should let this action run its course or should curb it is a matter that needs to be considered. When it comes to curbing it, we can get the following two effects from the minds of economists and authorities. First, to preserve China's existing silver. Second, to stop the fall in prices. The Chinese government has shown great patience on this issue. Because they saw silver flowing out, and they also acknowledged the outflow of capital – not only limited to foreigners, but also Chinese people shipping it abroad. They are in a difficult position, because if they allow silver to flow out without restriction, we will wake up one morning and find that we are all on a paper standard. All current banknotes cannot be redeemed, and there is only one way to sell goods, which is to use banknotes.

About ten days ago, another 25 million yuan in cash was shipped out, and another batch of 9.5 million yuan was being packed for shipment. Later, the government's tax order was issued, so the export of silver stopped – I cannot say it was prohibited.

The authorities have considered three plans regarding the silver issue. First, to ban the export of silver, but everyone thought this plan was inappropriate, and I also thought it was very right, because banning the export of silver might lead to worse results. Second, to increase the export tax, which is the plan that is currently being implemented. Third, is a very interesting question, which is to abolish silver coins and introduce the gold standard to China.

China adopting the gold standard would originally be a very good thing, but at present, there is no preparation at all. Everyone recalls the 1929 Kemmerer Commission's recommendations on this point, and their conclusion that it could not be implemented immediately, and it will become clear. Because China does not have the necessary gold reserves, and the provinces of China cannot be fully united to implement this plan.

Regarding this point, everyone should pay attention to the importance of the Kemmerer Commission. Because as a result of their work, the current gold unit was created. This system works very well, otherwise China's finances would have been on the verge of bankruptcy, and in 1930, 1931, and 1932, China's tariff revenue would never have been able to offset foreign debt. But it is impossible to adopt the gold standard at this moment. Even in the last few moments, I am afraid it will not work. The reasons are as follows: First, China has never stored enough gold coins; second, I don't believe that China can currently obtain enough gold coins to start implementing the gold standard. Many contemporary people have made many suggestions on this issue. Among them, Mr. Gu Jigao of China State Bank advocated that if the price of silver rises extremely high, China might as well use this opportunity to sell silver and exchange it for gold. This idea is very good, but it is difficult to implement. Because all the silver that China has today does not belong to the government.

Everyone knows that the currency reserves in the US and the Bank of England are government property; but when you talk about China's silver, 99 percent does not belong to the government. Therefore, I think nationalizing silver is impossible at the moment. In my personal opinion, the United States is bound by laws and morals to continue its policy of raising silver prices in the next four or five years. The price of silver overseas will inevitably rise sharply as a result. It will not be surprising if the price of silver rises to 70 or 80 cents US after not thinking about it for a long time. I believe that China may one day get the opportunity to profit from exchanging silver for gold, and at the same time put its currency on a gold basis. But this is a matter for the future, we need to calculate the reality, and discuss what kind of situation we are going to encounter now.

The first effect of increasing the silver export tax at this moment was that there was no movement in the market on the first day, but on the second day, the third day, and the fourth day, a danger occurred. I have rarely seen a precedent for this kind of situation. As for myself, many people have called me to ask for my opinion, and I have always answered them: "I don't know anything; I don't think about anything; I don't plan to do anything." This is my imitation of a lecturer's answer to a question twenty years ago. His answer was: "I can tell you definitively, one mistake, silver is going to rise or fall!"

I can say without hesitation that silver is going to rise. So a question comes up, what will China do if the price of silver rises sharply? We have now broken away from silver except domestically. We are already on an active paper currency standard, so if the price of silver rises, we must follow it very, very slowly. But I don't want a high standard. Judging from the situation in the past two days (October 17th and 18th), it has created a panic for speculators to offset the short positions they have thrown out. So it is best to have a healthy and very low standard, but I don't believe that this will help China's export trade, or that this limit can save China from difficulties.

There are many people who have suggested ways to help China solve this problem. I also have a plan, which is to ban the import of foreign rice. If the import of foreign rice can be stopped, I think the trade deficit can be eliminated. In the past three or four years, China has imported foreign rice with an average annual value of 100 million silver dollars. Just this number is enough to balance the trade deficit. Moreover, as far as I can see, this will definitely not cause people to starve to death. This is an obvious fact that China's rice yield per acre is only half of that of Japan, which shows that the methods used and the fertilizers applied in China lack modern scientific improvements. Not only that, due to traffic congestion and transportation difficulties, China's rice cannot circulate freely. It is said that shipping rice from Saigon to Shanghai is cheaper than shipping it from Wuxi to Shanghai. These facts are closely related to the issues we are discussing today.

We are now in the midst of a monetary panic, and the question is what we should do. I believe that if we calm down, we can easily return to the base of one shilling and five pence or one shilling and six pence. I think this base is most suitable for the trade in this port. This is very easy to achieve. I urge everyone not to believe the rumors in the market, and rush into the dangerous whirlpool. I am convinced that the current situation, based on today's environment, is not serious at all. If new methods and new laws are promulgated one after another tomorrow, then the old situation will of course change completely. As for the current situation, there is no need to panic at all. I hope everyone will maintain a calm mind, which is the most important thing in the current period of panic.

Discussion on the Construction of Railway Warehouses 213

— Wu Shaozeng

The Ministry of Railways considers circulating goods and developing the interior as one of its missions. Now, as the rural areas of the interior are on the verge of collapse, the railways should do what they can to provide indirect relief. Following the implementation of responsible freight transportation and responsible water and land combined transportation, in May of the 23rd year, a telegram was sent to various lines ordering them to add freight warehouses. The main points of the original telegram can be analyzed as follows:

Purpose: To assist in the activities of the rural economy, so that industry and commerce can develop in conjunction, and to prevent the imbalance of finance in various regions.

Plan: Focus on constructing freight warehouses at various stations to store excess agricultural products and to allow for loans secured by goods as collateral, so as to facilitate turnover and make railway freight transportation increasingly prosperous.

Warehouse Nature

(1) Ordinary storage: Specifically for cargo owners to store goods on a regular basis, with a small storage fee charged.

(2) Transportation storage: Specifically for goods that have already been accepted for transportation but have not yet been shipped out, for temporary storage, with no storage fee charged.

(3) There is no need to distinguish between ordinary storage and transportation storage during construction, but management should be distinguished according to their nature.

Handling Guidelines

(1) Select a number of stations with the most freight volume, the most urgent need for warehouses, and the potential for merchants to use goods as collateral for loans in the future.

(2) Predict the maximum amount of cargo entering, exiting, and stockpiling at the above stations within the next ten years.

(3) Formulate an overall plan for the construction of freight warehouses over the next ten years, to be implemented year by year.

(4) For the part needed this year, prepare a construction budget according to the standard drawings issued by the Ministry.

(5) The location should be connected and able to accommodate entire trains for loading and unloading.

(6) Consideration should be given to the turnouts for shunting and parking vehicles, so that vehicle operation can be economical.

According to the mission of the railway to circulate goods, it should not simply end with transporting goods from the departure station to the arrival station. The railway cannot but properly store goods that are reported for transportation at the departure station but cannot be loaded immediately; the railway also cannot but properly store goods that have arrived at the arrival station but cannot be immediately taken out or put on the market. Although this type of storage is subject to a certain time limit, so as not to allow long-term stockpiling, which would hinder the storage of later goods, its nature is actually a part of the meaning included in railway transportation. If the railway does not also handle the storage of goods, it cannot fulfill its transportation responsibility. This is what is called transportation storage, or short-term storage, which is actually a direct business of the railway. As for goods that are stored in railway warehouses because they are not intended to be transported and sold urgently, or stockpiled to wait for the right time to seek a good price, or "pledged for loans to facilitate turnover," this is what is called ordinary storage, or long-term storage. According to its nature, it is very different from transportation storage and cannot be said to have any related responsibility to the railway transportation itself. Even if the railway has this ability and can handle it, it is an indirect rather than a direct business, which is undoubtedly clear based on common sense. Moreover, according to Article 613 of the Civil Law, "A warehouse operator is a person who, for remuneration, engages in the business of storing and safekeeping goods for others," and Article 622, "A carrier is a person who engages in the business of transporting goods or passengers and receives freight." Now the railway belongs to the carrier, and is therefore different from the warehouse operator.

Based on the above discussion, since transportation storage is a direct business of the railway, it is indeed necessary for the railway to directly handle it. Therefore, all lines that do not have warehouse facilities, or whose capacity is too small, or whose distribution is not adequate to meet the needs, should follow the instructions of the Ministry's telegram and actively add facilities, at least to meet the needs of transportation storage. As for ordinary storage warehouses, which are used for long-term storage of goods, since they are not a direct business of the railway, whether they should also be directly handled by the railway seems to be open to discussion.

The purpose of the banking industry in constructing warehouses is no more than two items: one is to operate warehousing business, and the other is to handle mortgage loans. For banks, it opens up a way to invest and generate profits, and for merchants, it provides convenience for turnover and finance. Therefore, it is not impossible to say that ordinary storage is a direct business of the bank. As for the railway's ordinary storage, it seems that it does not necessarily have to be directly handled, and there are two reasons for this:

(1) In terms of funding, operating large-scale warehouses is expensive. The railway's main business is transportation, and all capital should of course be invested in rolling stock equipment as a priority. It is difficult to use huge sums of money for warehouses. Moreover, most of our country's railways are built with foreign capital, and their operating income, in addition to all expenses, should also be used to repay principal and pay interest, which is even more difficult to sustain. It is not easy to expand or renovate rolling stock equipment, so how can there be surplus capacity for large-scale ordinary storage warehouses?

(2) In terms of talent, large-scale ordinary storage warehouses, such as various insulation, cooling, and ventilation devices in the cold storage department; such as conveying machine devices and hoisting machine devices in the grain unloading warehouse; cleaning machines, mixing machines, grinding machines, and various devices in the milling workshop; and other warehouse compression devices, packaging devices, canning devices, etc., all belong to specialized technologies. The railway's original talent is mostly biased towards rolling stock transportation. If it is desired to operate ordinary storage warehouses, it is necessary to add specialized talent, which is not allowed by the current financial resources. If the original talent is used to deal with this special business, although temporary planning and supervision can be entrusted to engineering experts to handle, it will be difficult to be competent and happy in the regular management work.

Therefore, the matter of ordinary storage, whether observed from a theoretical or factual perspective, feels that it is better for merchants to handle it than for the railway to handle it, and it is most appropriate for it to be handled by the banking industry. However, no matter what, the warehouse facilities required along the railway line are closely related to railway transportation after all, and the railway cannot only handle transportation storage and ignore ordinary storage. The compromise solution is to divide railway warehouses into four major categories:

The first category is simple transportation warehouses. At stations with sparse freight, the railway only carries sporadic items and packages, and the customers only need simple transportation storage. This type of warehouse has a very simple structure, limited cost, and easy management, and it is also something that the railway must have. Of course, the railway should invest in building it and be responsible for its management.

The second category is mixed transportation and ordinary warehouses. At stations with relatively heavy freight, some only need transportation storage, and some also need ordinary storage. This type of warehouse can be divided into two halves, one for transportation storage and one for ordinary storage; the part belonging to ordinary storage can also be divided into several parts according to the type of goods, so as to store them separately. This type of mixed warehouse is of course more convenient to manage centrally, and the railway should also invest in building it. Fortunately, the scale is not large, the management is easier, and the cost is still limited.

The third category is divided transportation and ordinary warehouses. At stations with very heavy freight, there is a large amount of transportation storage needed, and there is also a large amount of ordinary storage needed, so it is necessary to build transportation warehouses and ordinary warehouses separately. In this case, the transportation warehouse part should of course be invested in and built by the railway, which need not be repeated. There are several possible solutions to the ordinary warehouse problem:

(A) The railway invests in construction and manages it itself;

(B) The railway invests in construction and merchants rent it for operation;

(C) The merchants invest in construction and the railway rents it for operation;

(D) The merchants invest in construction and manage it themselves.

However, for railways with tight financial resources, it may still be most appropriate to adopt method (D). The reasons for this, in addition to the above-mentioned funding and talent, there is another point; if the ordinary warehouses along the railway line are directly operated by banks, then in the event of pledging goods for loans, the bank can easily check, determine the amount of the loan, and easily handle it, so that they can have the certainty of taking it back, so why not do it. And for merchants, on the one hand, they stockpile goods to wait for a good price, and on the other hand, they pledge loans to make other deals, which is tantamount to using a capital of one thousand yuan to do business of several thousand yuan, so why not do it. If this is the case, not only can the railway bill of lading be promoted as much as possible, but its freight transportation will also inevitably develop day by day, which can be asserted. Conversely, if the railway itself operates ordinary warehouses, since it cannot also handle large-scale loans, it cannot achieve this great effect.

The fourth category is simple ordinary storage. Although this type of storage is usually called a warehouse, in fact, in addition to storing goods, it also has the following special functions:

(A) Intermediate assembly: The railway allows the consignor to gradually concentrate less-than-carload goods at the locations it passes through, in order to load them into a whole car in the future and transport them to the destination, without affecting its full-journey freight rate.

(B) Intermediate compression: The railway allows the consignor to unload hay, rice stalks, wheat stalks, cotton, and other items at a certain location it passes through, and then incorporate them into the whole car after reducing the volume, and transport them to the destination.

(C) Intermediate warehousing: The railway allows the consignor to unload rice into the intermediate grain warehouse to wait for mixing, bleaching, soil removal, air drying, grading, bagging, weighing, and re-transporting, without affecting its full-journey freight rate.

(D) Intermediate grinding: The railway allows the consignor to unload wheat and other items in the middle and grind them into flour before transporting them out.

(E) Intermediate packing: The railway allows the consignor to unload oil in the middle and pack it into large barrels or drum-shaped containers for re-transporting, etc.

All of this is what the United States calls special transportation business, which is also needed in our country at present but has not yet been implemented. This type of warehouse is very large in scale, extremely expensive, and the management work is also very heavy. Judging from the current situation of our country's railways, it is definitely difficult to be competent, so it should be independently built by merchants and managed by merchants themselves.

As for its location, it is most suitable to be about halfway along the railway line from the main production area to the main consumption area, such as Benniu on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and other similar places. Because the land price is low and the wages are cheap, the cost of building a sales warehouse here is much lower than in Wuxi, Shanghai, and other places; and it is easier to start expanding at any time according to needs than in Wuxi, Shanghai, and other places. This is one of the reasons.

If a large amount of goods is directly transported from the production area to the consumer market, at the departure station, one already feels the large number of parking spaces occupied and the huge freight cost, and when arriving at the arrival station, if it cannot be sold immediately and must be stored in a warehouse, one must also feel the large number of storage spaces occupied and the huge storage rent cost. If there is such a large-scale warehouse and workshop in the middle, so that goods can be unloaded in the middle, sporadic ones can be combined, huge ones can be compressed, rice grains can be removed from their bran, coarse cotton can be rolled into fine cotton, wheat can be ground into flour, copper and iron can be cast into bars, etc., the storage and manufacturing costs are lower than in the city, and the manufactured products are re-transported, the parking spaces occupied are smaller, and the freight costs are less. When they are transported to the market, they can be sold immediately. What is the economic convenience like? This is the second reason.

From the railway's point of view, the raw materials transported occupy more parking spaces, and the freight collected is of course more, but the grades of the manufactured products are higher. Although the parking spaces occupied are smaller, the loss is negligible when the two are compared. According to the principle of railway transportation, it is better to transport more manufactured products than to transport more raw materials. The former costs more parking spaces and requires more vehicles; the latter saves parking spaces and can use one vehicle for two, which is very economical for equipment, especially for railways with insufficient financial resources. Moreover, if there are such warehouses and workshops along the railway line, all kinds of goods will be happy with its convenience and will inevitably gather together. The railway only needs to lay turnouts to control them and set appropriate freight rates to attract them, and there is no need to worry about the competitive forces of other transportation businesses. This is the third reason.

Recently, the railway authorities have been making every effort to promote responsible freight transportation. If the railway does not properly plan for the storage of goods, it will not be able to complete the mission of responsible transportation. However, after carefully studying the meaning of the above-mentioned telegram from the Ministry of Railways, it has moved from the first type of warehouse mentioned above to seeking the realization of the second type of warehouse. However, according to the needs of customers, I am afraid that they are not satisfied with the second type of warehouse, but expect the construction of the third and even fourth type of warehouses; it seems that it is easier to realize by inviting businesses and banks to invest in construction, and the railway provides freight sidings and other conveniences, and both parties fully cooperate.

Someone may say; Merchants have always held the principle of profit-seeking. If ordinary storage is assigned to merchants, then not only will this business be monopolized by them, but the railway may also be controlled by them. If the entire future of transportation is greatly affected as a result, it will inevitably outweigh the gains. However, this is an overestimation. The evils of monopoly are mostly the result of exclusive patents. Any business, if it has a little competition, there is no monopoly to speak of. Therefore, the railway only needs to assign the ordinary storage warehouses along the line to several banks to handle, and there will definitely be no monopoly. For the sake of simplicity, the railway can ask the banks to jointly form a banking syndicate to take over the large-scale warehouses needed along the line, which is easier to realize; since banks have become a group under this kind of facility, it seems difficult to avoid monopolistic behavior; however, every business aims at profit, and operating warehouses is no exception. If the goal is profit, the higher the price, the fewer the transactions, and the lower the price, the more the transactions. This is an immutable principle in economics. Therefore, enlightened merchants will choose the price that is most attractive to transactions and can obtain the most profit as the standard. And the price that is most attractive to transactions is definitely not the highest price; if the lowest price is set to attract the most and widest transactions, it is especially a win-win situation. Moreover, each bank has its own interests and restrains each other. Therefore, even if the banking syndicate intends to monopolize the warehouse, there will not be a monopoly in fact. Otherwise, the transactions will be depressed, which is called self-defeating, and the merchants will not do this.

As for controlling the railway, it is even more seemingly correct but actually wrong. Since merchants build warehouses along the railway line, they need the help of the railway everywhere. Therefore, their psychology must be full of the hope that the railway will cooperate with them. How can they use this to control the railway and lead to the danger that the railway will not cooperate with them. Because the merchants' warehouses and the railway's transportation have a related relationship, only full cooperation between the two parties can achieve the goal of coexistence and mutual benefit; otherwise, both will be hurt, and merchants are well aware of the advantages and disadvantages, and will definitely not fail to see this. Then the railway's assignment of ordinary storage to merchants can lead the way for cooperation between the railway and the financial community; one day, the financial community will develop a strong interest in the railway business, and then take a step further, willing to provide the railway with various economic assistance, which is also unknown.

Now the Ministry of Railways is investigating and evaluating the situation of the original warehouses of the state-owned railways in various countries, the current freight transportation needs, and the entire plan for the future. Therefore, I will briefly write one or two points as far as my humble opinion can reach, to provide materials for discussion. I know that flaws and omissions are inevitable, and I hope that railway experts and enlightened people from all parties will correct them (End)

Finance: Quiet Sunday Foreign Exchange Market 214

Silver Dollars Plunged, Copper Coins Rose Slightly

Yesterday, because it was Sunday and banks were closed as usual, the foreign exchange market was quiet. Only some money shops were still open as usual. The interbank price of silver dollars in the market was 6 fen in both the morning and afternoon markets, with no difference from the previous day. In terms of clearing transactions, more than 2.5 million yuan was transferred in the morning market, more than 600,000 yuan in new transactions, more than 400,000 yuan in the afternoon market, more than 300,000 yuan in the Small General Association, and more than 300,000 yuan in foreign exchange mortgage transactions were redeemed, with no new transactions heard. Bank collections and disbursements were suspended due to the holiday. Only money shops collected and disbursed more than 37 million yuan in foreign exchange official bills. As for subsidiary coins, although small silver dollar transactions were smooth, prices fell due to remittances. Jiangnan small silver dollars once fell to 8 yuan in the morning market, to 825 yuan. Although they rebounded by 2 yuan in the afternoon market, to 837 yuan, the result was a fall of 6 yuan from the previous day. In terms of executed transactions, 11,000 jiao were traded in the morning market and 5,000 jiao in the afternoon market. Guangdong small silver dollars fell by 1.8 yuan in the morning market, to 748 yuan, and continued to fall by 0.5 yuan in the afternoon market, to 747.5 yuan. The result was a fall of 2.3 yuan from the previous day. In terms of executed transactions, 165,000 jiao were traded in the morning market and 90,000 jiao in the afternoon market. Copper coins alone rose by 500 wen due to supply exceeding demand, to 323,500 wen. The transaction price was 12,800 yuan in silver dollars, equivalent to 41,408 strings of wen.

Securities 215

Securities Prices Rose Over the Week

Over the past week (October 15th to 20th), the bond market of the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange has experienced quite a storm. It has been brewing for a long time, and occasionally encounters an impact, causing turbulent waves and a boiling market. The entire Shanghai Exchange was shocked. The implementation of the silver tax suddenly came into effect. What is the relationship between this issue and the market price of public bonds? At first, it was considered ambiguous, then it was thought that the currency was cheap and things were expensive, and then there were still many misunderstandings. The market price of the exchange also fluctuated greatly, causing a great uproar. According to the silver tax, the outflow of cash will naturally decrease, or even stop because of this. People's hearts are becoming more and more excited. However, because the settlement period is approaching, the market price cannot temporarily tend to a level. Over the past week, the silver tax issue has been implemented on Monday, but the market price only rose by half a yuan at the beginning. After that, rumors rose again, and the price gradually increased, still only a small amount of 3-4 jiao. On Tuesday, although the rumors subsided, people were still uneasy, and it was slightly better by about half a yuan. On Wednesday, bulls came out, or rolled over, still a small amount of 3-4 jiao. Three days after the silver tax, the public bond market did not have any stimulation. On Thursday, due to the saying of paper currency policy, most of the Shanghai exchanges rose to the limit in the early session. The public bond price was still hovering in the early session, and began to rise wildly in the second session. The market was suddenly tense, and the popularity was extremely high, rising by 2 yuan in one day. On Friday, the large bulls came out, and most of them misunderstood the silver issue. The market price fell by about 1 yuan. On Saturday, it was heard that the Fifth Plenary Session would not be postponed, and the southwest was taken over, and the situation was very satisfactory. Hu Zhantang also had the saying of coming to Beijing, and the market price rose by about half a yuan. Judging from the recent situation, there are still many shorts in the market, and the Fifth Plenary Session will definitely be successful. In the past few weeks, there have been many people who are bearish, and the short positions have actually been quite a lot. Therefore, at this time when the settlement is approaching, the news is good, and the bond market still has a short squeeze. As a result of the market price for a week, it is estimated that the increase ranges from a few jiao to 1.67 yuan. The total number of transactions totaled 129,585,000 yuan, and 250 shares of stock. Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

The Tragic Fire on Avenue Edward VII 219

— A Family

This is truly "shocking": fifteen people were burned alive in the fire all at once! According to reports, there were originally fourteen victims, but one of them was a pregnant woman, Ms. So-and-so. Counting the seven-month-old fetus, the total is indeed fifteen. In addition, there were five people with burns. And they, both men and women, were all "one family"! Although they had different surnames and included eight (plus the "subletter"). The front building, the back building, the attic, the front and back annexes, the kitchen, the drying platform, etc., with men, women, the old, and the young, totaling nineteen people, but they were all living together in a two-story, single-family market building. Thus, such a major tragedy unfolded in an instant!

However, the fact that such a small house was packed to the brim shows the "prosperity" and "population density" of Shanghai, doesn't it? Indeed, this place can be called the "New York of the East"! According to a recent report published by the Public Works Department of the Public Concession, the total investment in construction in the Public Concession and the French Concession in the past ten years amounted to a staggering 466.7 million yuan. Last year, the number of high-rise buildings in the Public Concession increased by 879, and the French Concession saw an even greater increase of more than 900. However, the fact that nearly thirty people lived in one single-family house truly demonstrates the "flourishing" state of this "New York of the East," doesn't it? But on the other hand, if we pay closer attention, we will be somewhat disappointed. According to the statistics of the Finance Department of the Public Concession Bureau, the number of vacant houses in the Public Concession alone is as high as 5,383. In the same period of the twenty-first year, it was 4,687. If we add the vacant houses in the French Concession and the South City, the number would probably be no less than ten thousand!

In such a comparison, we must realize that, on the one hand, in today's cities, investment in construction and real estate remains one of the good business sectors for entrepreneurs. However, on the other hand, due to external multi-faceted aggression by various capitalist imperialists and the impact of the "world economic panic," and internal rural economic bankruptcy, market decline, and various "recession" phenomena, the trend is only becoming more widespread and profound. Thus, high-rise empty buildings are allowed to increase by the thousands to show the prosperity of the "New York of the East"?

Occasional Notes from the Study 220

— Philosopher

(1) A Humble Sentiment

The speed of the century's progress is truly too fast. Being violently thrown onto the street corner, caught in the various problems rushing in from all directions, one only feels that they cannot even stand firm in the torrent of life, constantly surfacing in the whirlpool. Perhaps they will drown soon? Faced with the kaleidoscopic and colorful aspects of life, one is too fragile. But what can temper people into camels capable of enduring hardship and humiliation? On the one hand, it is the suffering of life, and on the other hand, isn't it those books left behind by human ancestors, books that shine with the light of wisdom? In order to make oneself stronger, one has long yearned for a simple study filled with books. This is not a luxurious hope. I don't want precious stationery or ornate bookshelves. The study I speak of is just a small room, a willow wood table, a few shelves of beloved books, a writing brush, a bottle of ink, and a few sheets of rough paper. My desires are also very humble. If I could boil a pot of coffee, light a dish of benzoin on the table, and have two hours each day without being disturbed by anything, giving me some peace to leisurely face the books, what happiness that would be! Besides the time and energy given to society, people should reserve some time and energy for themselves to enjoy. But in this cruel world, besides the time and energy consumed for life, no, I mean wasted for necessary survival, how much can be saved for oneself to do something non-professional, something one loves?

That tiny happiness is also taken away from us salaried workers.

For the past few years, my dream has been to build my own little world in this vast world, to build a study. Truly a pitiful animal without the ability to control one's own life as one wishes. Constant effort has only resulted in an old table and half a shelf of miscellaneous old books, with a bit of everything. I am actually satisfied with these things, if only I could sit at the table and, of my own will, flip through this book, move that book. Although it is such an easy thing to do, it has not been done yet. Only on the road, on the bus, while rushing around for food and clothing, can I snatch some time to hastily read some books.

Because of this, I have a cursing attitude towards life. The two hours spent in the study should always be given to me.

It's not just my situation that's like this. There are many, many people like me in the group around me, even some who are worse off than me. Only my friend So-and-so is an exception. He is a bachelor. In his residence, unlike others, he turned a small room of less than one square zhang into a bedroom, while he turned a spacious and bright room into a exquisite study. This is probably because he is an intellectual. Every time I walk into his study, see the walls filled with books, and stand in front of the bookshelf, flipping through the books one by one, feelings of envy always involuntarily surge up. When I sit down on the sofa next to the desk, holding that crystal lion-shaped paperweight in my hand and playing with it, my friend will smile triumphantly.

What can be done about such a smile? One can only sigh helplessly from the bottom of one's heart. Then my friend, as usual——

"I've poured all my heart and soul and income into this over the years!" He would begin by saying such things, then go on to talk in detail about how he bought Joyce's Ulysses from an old bookstore for seventy cents, how he saved half a month's transportation money for that hardcover, and so on.

He has already told such stories in front of me five or six times, but every time I step into his study, he never tires of repeating them. Even if I have heard it a hundred times, I can still find new interest and new joy in this old story.

Rural Sketch: Going to Town with Grandfather for Tea 221

Page 21

Pleasure. Returning home and seeing my own dilapidated desk and dust-covered books, I always rekindle my ambition to build a study, and at the same time:

"When will I be able to sit at the desk and quietly hold the book in my heart?" I lament in this way, and this will probably become a lifelong sentiment.

To a Village Friend 222

— Lie

Although I have been in Shanghai for a full seven years, if you suddenly ask me, "What is Shanghai really like?" I would be at a loss for words. This is why I have had your letter for two weeks and have left it on my desk without replying. Today, after the heavy rain, I stood by the window, looking at the flying clouds and thinking of old friends. Then, I felt guilty for not replying to my friend's letter. So, I concentrated my mind and thought about the question, "What is Shanghai really like?" over and over again for twenty-eight minutes and five seconds, but I still cannot give a correct and definite answer.

Is Shanghai good? I dare not readily affirm. Is Shanghai bad? I also disagree by more than sixty percent. Shanghai, as I see it, is truly full of the flavor of dissecting phenomena using dialectics. What does this mean? We know that Shanghai is a gathering place for the unemployed, but there are also many job opportunities. Shanghai can force people to death, but it can also save people. There is a dark side, and there is also a bright side. There are bad people, and there are also good people. This is my understanding of Shanghai over the past seven years, and it can be considered a general critique of it.

You also ask, "Can I come to Shanghai? If I come, can I avoid starvation?" I can only give a humorous answer, "Starving is up to you, not starving is also up to you."

From one perspective, Shanghai is a professional looting field watched by all eyes. You rob me and I rob you, but it is all for the sake of "too many monks, too little gruel" and "too many people for the available positions." Thus, bit by bit, yesterday one, today two, either jumping into the Huangpu River, or committing suicide by poisoning, or... although the ways of dying are inconsistent, the numbers are extremely alarming. These suicides are, of course, a blatant explanation of why Shanghai is Shanghai. Secondly, there are still many people whose life force has not yet been cut off, struggling in the extreme pain of unemployment, craning their necks and reaching their heads, never finding a single job all year round, never getting a scoop of porridge all day long. Thus, beggars are everywhere, and the starving fill the roads, not dying by suicide, but dying by starvation.

Another way of saying it is that Shanghai is also a living Shanghai. As long as a person has a skill and encounters an opportunity, they can live very well. And sometimes they can even rise to prominence, dominating one side. Looking back, people like Hartung, Ye Chengzhong, and more recently So-and-so and XX, all rose up in Shanghai with their bare hands. Naturally, there are also powerful people who value you, support you, so that you don't starve, don't lose your job, and can live and develop. Looking back, there are also many people who pick up cigarette butts or find a living in the garbage dump. As for those hooligans and bums, they can also live their days comfortably. In short, Shanghai is very livable. Even if you are unemployed, it is still very livable. If you are healthy and encounter some opportunities, it is even easier to live.

As I see it, Shanghai is such a Shanghai. Are you coming? I won't stop you. Are you not coming? I won't urge you either.

Sick 223

— Menglan

The sicker, the poorer,

The poorer, the sicker,

Sick and poor, poor and sick.

Page 22

Page 23

I wrote such a short poem three years ago, and now, lying on my sickbed, I think of it again.

I never thought that although three years have flown by, everything is still the same. The so-called progress is probably just that poverty and illness are progressing, right?

What will it be like after three more years? I dare not think about it anymore. But on the sickbed, when tossing and turning sleeplessly, such thoughts inevitably turn cold again.

For poor fellows like us who work all day to eat three meals, we can barely cope when we are as strong as oxen. But once we get sick, not to mention that we have to scrape together medical expenses, we also have to find a way to fill this stomach. Therefore, while drinking the bitter medicine, I worry about when I will be able to repay this debt.

I have friends, and indeed many friends who are willing to help financially. However, there are not many wealthy friends. Those who are have long gone to enjoy wealth and glory and make friends with other wealthy people. Those who are left and willing to help financially are only friends who are as poor as I am, eating today's meal and having to prepare for where the money for tomorrow's meal will come from.

When sick, emotions become abnormally fragile, very easily angered, and often inexplicably bursting into tears. But for some reason, one feels that everything is meaningless, unwilling to drink medicine, just quietly waiting to taste the flavor of death. But when one discovers that there are only a few copper coins left in the drawer, and one has to pick out clothes that are not needed for the time being from the box to exchange for money, one has to sit up and pick up a pen to write black characters on white paper.

When emotions fluctuate more unpredictably than autumn clouds, the first to bear the brunt is naturally the wife. Some extremely minor disagreements will provoke my inexplicable anger. The wife, in such a situation, does not resist, nor does she answer, but, like a captured prisoner, bows her head and says nothing, or turns her back and secretly wipes away her tears with a handkerchief. When my anger subsides, she quietly sits by the bed, thinking absentmindedly, or staring absently at the autumn clouds outside the window. Afterwards, when her emotions have calmed down, she leans close to my ear and asks, "What do you want to eat? You!"

At the same time, she reaches into the drawer to count her money. When the wife's back disappears before my eyes, I often feel inexplicably lost.

East, West, North, South 224

— San Duo

Shanghai is worthy of being the largest metropolis in East Asia, with British territory, French territory, and Chinese territory. Twenty-four-story buildings pierce the gray sky. The "Full" sign is always hanging in front of the hotels. Jai alai, dog racing, banknotes turn into colored paper and flutter in the air. And! Do you know? The stage of 1935 will be crowned on an auspicious day!

And? Of course there is! The fire on Avenue Edward VII; the collapse of the Shanghai Industrial Bank!

This is heaven above hell!

The rural economy is bankrupt. In years of great harvest, grains are worthless; in years of great drought, the fields are full of rice stalks. The rent still has to be paid. So, dreaming of gold, they shoulder their baggage, step onto the ship, and bring their fate to the metropolis to seek a final verdict.

The recommendation shops are crowded with people. The factories are crowded with people. People, people, people are everywhere, forming this metropolis of three million people.

A well-dressed fat man walks out of a foreign-style house, holding a cigar, and is squeezed into a car by a tall White Russian, "beep beep"... the life of heaven!

Pale pink, pale green lights, women embracing snakes are intoxicated in the atmosphere of champagne, smiles swirling on everyone's faces, the life of heaven!

But who goes to hell?

The docks and stations are constantly sending off crowds of people with foreign accents, one, five, one hundred, one thousand, why don't they return?

Taking poison, throwing themselves into the river, creating materials for daily social newspapers!

Heaven and hell organize this largest metropolis in East Asia!

Amateur Mailbox

Can Patented Products Be Imitated? 225

Editor:

I have a matter that I would like to ask for guidance. I think you are a guide for those wandering on the wrong path, and you will not refuse me.

I and several friends have been researching a certain machine. After years of exploration and repeated experiments, we were finally successful. Now we want to register with the government agency in order to enjoy the right of patent. However, this kind of machine is very easy to imitate. If what I have created is a round shape, others can imitate it and create one dozen, and although the brand and shape are different, the function is the same. I don't know if I have the right to interfere with him? Is there any way to prevent others from imitating it? Please reply in the newspaper as soon as possible. Respectfully, Guan Xionghui

Wrote with peace

Editor's note: If you register with the government and obtain a patent, you have the right of invention and are protected by the government, and others may not imitate it. Because what the right of invention protects is the principle of the invention, not the form of the invention. Therefore, others, such as changing the appearance and imitating it, have the right to prevent it.

Storytelling in Suzhou Dialect 227

Central China (1040)

Yao Xiao'an, Pang Xueqing - "The Pearl Pagoda"

10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening (Lament of the Autumn Window)

A bolt from the blue is startling. Why harbor resentment and secretly harm people? I want to comfort and gladden my parents, to live an honest, thrifty life. (Last night) an unexpected letter suddenly arrived. (Therefore) I bid farewell hastily and returned home. Hearing my mother's words, my heart nearly breaks. Though untrue, it's hard to deny the claims. I've never frequented brothels or flower-lined streets, let alone actresses and entertainers. (I am) a respectable son of a prominent Fengxi family. (How could I) abandon my integrity and embrace modernity? Our family is poor, and I had little schooling. At just thirteen, I began to learn a trade. Sadly, I learned an unrelated profession. I lack knowledge and skill. I am grateful for the recommendations of my elders. I broadcast on the radio from a middle school. A year has passed in the blink of an eye, with neither profit nor loss for the company. (I hope) to flourish and improve daily, so that one day I can establish myself and succeed. Who knew this trouble would arise out of nowhere, causing me shame before my clan? (Saying that) there is no wind, no waves, (saying that) the shrimp doesn't jump, the water doesn't move, I will never be able to clear my name. I want to throw myself into the Pu River as a water ghost, but I have yet to repay my parents' nurturing kindness.

Central China (1040)

Guanyin Society - "The Gallant Maidens and Knights Errant"

7:15 PM to 8:00 PM

Oh no! What to do? Young Master An forgot his ancestral treasured inkstone at Nengren Temple! He thinks: my paternal grandfather's name is engraved on the inkstone! If this murder case is discovered, wouldn't it implicate him? He's desperately worried! But Thirteenth Sister comforts him, saying: Don't worry, leave it to me, I'll keep it safe for you. Then, weeping, they part ways!

The murder case at Nengren Temple is indeed discovered. The local magistrate, originally a sesame paste official, encountering such an unprecedented case, is bound to make many jokes! Listen attentively!

Hua Xing (1260)

Guanyin Society - "Dream of the Red Chamber: The Tragic History of the Two Yous"

8:15 PM to 9:00 PM

Liu Xianglian is said to be cold-hearted, which is indeed true. Somehow, he received news that Third Sister You's reputation was not good. So he ran to Jia Lian to return the sword and call off the engagement! Third Sister You is puzzled, she loves him no matter what. In the end, because of this, she used the engagement mandarin duck sword to commit suicide in front of Xianglian!

Lovers above all else, I think they must sigh with regret.

Yong Sheng (1080)

Guanyin Society - "Good Youth"

9:00 PM to 10:00 PM

It's true that ugly people often cause trouble. If you don't believe it, look at how Qiao Niang is back to her old ways! Poor Qiu Hong has become the object of her venting! Even a tiger doesn't eat its cubs, let alone a person with feelings! But Qiao Niang! She is even more cruel than beasts! She stained the delicate child's arm with crimson blood: is this kind of barbaric behavior something that humans can do?

Hua Mei (1060)

Guanyin Society - "The Fate of Tears and Laughter"

10:00 PM to 11:00 PM

General Liu and Xiugu's wedding ceremony was held in the Western Hills. General Liu's happiness was truly unexpected. An ancient temple on a mountain cliff was transformed into an unprecedented bridal chamber under the General's command. Candlelight illuminated the newlyweds, and sweet wine stirred their excitement. During their intimate moments, the General embraced a young woman, but... it turns out this was Xiugu's plan. The General's martial prowess finally parted from his stinky skin!

The great heroine Guan Xiugu, it's just a pity that she contains some feudal ideas!

Xin Sheng (1380)

Minsheng Society - "The Three Smiles"

10:00 PM to 11:00 PM

Tang Yin followed Qiu Xiang to the gate of the Donglin Hua Mansion in Wuxi. He saw Qiu Xiang cast a third loving glance. The three smiles showed affection. Alas, he could not enter. In desperation, he exchanged clothes with the boatman, claiming to be visiting relatives but was turned away. Coincidentally, the Hua Mansion was hiring a book boy. He was introduced to the Grand Tutor by the steward Wang Jin, sold himself as a servant, and changed his name to Hua An. From then on, the scholar became a servant.

News 229

The Yuanchang Advertising Company Broadcasting Station, located at 323 Annachang Road in this city, is publishing the complete "Sister Flowers" radio drama script. They are expanding their publicity. They held an unprecedented event at the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Radio Station. The author of the book, Mr. Li Changjian, heard the cyclical special program of singing and opera. They also started pre-sales during the broadcast of the special program. The entire book contains 300,000 words and is priced at 80 cents. Pre-orders are only 48 cents, and a personally signed photo and couplet by Mr. Li Changjian will be added. The entire book has now been printed and is on sale. There is an outer cover by Mr. Jia Ni Qiongxian and an inner cover by Mr. Yang Yixing. The special price of 72 cents will still be sold before the end of this month. There is also a popular edition that sells for 54 cents.
